<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable plainlinks">This is a <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Lists#Incomplete_lists" title="Wikipedia:WikiProject Lists">dynamic list</a> and may never be able to satisfy particular standards for completeness. You can help by <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_company_name_etymologies&amp;action=edit">expanding it</a> with <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Reliable sources">reliably sourced</a> entries.</div>
<p>This is a list of company names with their name origins explained. Some of the origins are disputed.
</p>

<h2><span id="0.E2.80.939"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="0–9">0–9</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_company_name_etymologies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: 0–9">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/19_Entertainment" title="19 Entertainment">19 Entertainment</a> – talent company founded by <a href="/wiki/Simon_Fuller" title="Simon Fuller">Simon Fuller</a> and "named after Paul Hardcastle's single 19, the first No. 1 Fuller had a hand in", according to <i>TV Guide</i><sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> After selling 19 Entertainment to <a href="/wiki/CKX,_Inc" class="mw-redirect" title="CKX, Inc">CKX, Inc</a>, Fuller founded <a href="/wiki/XIX_Entertainment" title="XIX Entertainment">XIX Entertainment</a>, which is 19 in Roman numerals.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/20th_Century_Fox" title="20th Century Fox">20th Century Fox</a> – film studio; formed in 1935 through the merger of <a href="/wiki/William_Fox_(producer)" title="William Fox (producer)">William Fox</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Fox_Film" title="Fox Film">Fox Film</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Twentieth_Century_Pictures" title="Twentieth Century Pictures">Twentieth Century Pictures</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/21st_Century_Fox" title="21st Century Fox">21st Century Fox</a> – media company formed by spinning off <a href="/wiki/News_Corporation_(1980%E2%80%932013)" title="News Corporation (1980–2013)">News Corporation</a>'s TV and movie properties in 2013. It owns <a href="/wiki/20th_Century_Fox" title="20th Century Fox">20th Century Fox</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Fox_Broadcasting_Company" title="Fox Broadcasting Company">Fox Broadcasting Company</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fox_News" title="Fox News">Fox News</a>, <a href="/wiki/Star_TV_(Asian_TV_networks)" title="Star TV (Asian TV networks)">Star TV</a> and others.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/23andMe" title="23andMe">23andMe</a> – using the 23 pairs of chromosomes that make up each person's <a href="/wiki/Genome" title="Genome">genome</a>, the company helps individuals make sense of their own genome.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/27b/6" class="mw-redirect" title="27b/6">27b/6</a> – apartment where <a href="/wiki/George_Orwell" title="George Orwell">George Orwell</a> wrote the novel <i><a href="/wiki/Nineteen_Eighty-Four" title="Nineteen Eighty-Four">Nineteen Eighty-Four</a></i> was number 27B on level 6.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/37signals" class="mw-redirect" title="37signals">37signals</a> – web development company; named for the 37 <a href="/wiki/Radiotelescope" class="mw-redirect" title="Radiotelescope">radiotelescope</a> signals identified by astronomer <a href="/wiki/Paul_Horowitz" title="Paul Horowitz">Paul Horowitz</a> as potential messages from <a href="/wiki/Extraterrestrial_intelligence" title="Extraterrestrial intelligence">extraterrestrial intelligence</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> In 2014, the company renamed itself Basecamp, after its main product.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/3Com" title="3Com">3Com</a> – network technology producer; the three <i>com</i>s are computer, communication, and compatibility.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/3dfx_Interactive" title="3dfx Interactive">3dfx Interactive</a> – 3d and fx, standing for "three-dimensional effects".</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/3M" title="3M">3M</a> – from the company's original name, Minnesota Mining and Manufacturing Company.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/7-Eleven" title="7-Eleven">7-Eleven</a> – convenience stores; renamed from "Tote'm" in 1946 to reflect their newly extended hours, 7:00&nbsp;am until 11:00&nbsp;pm.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="A">A</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_company_name_etymologies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: A">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/A%26M_Records" title="A&amp;M Records">A&amp;M Records</a> – named after founders <a href="/wiki/Herb_Alpert" title="Herb Alpert">Herb Alpert</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Moss" title="Jerry Moss">Jerry Moss</a><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Great_Atlantic_and_Pacific_Tea_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Atlantic and Pacific Tea Company">A&amp;P</a> – from Atlantic &amp; Pacific in <a href="/wiki/Great_Atlantic_and_Pacific_Tea_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Atlantic and Pacific Tea Company">Great Atlantic and Pacific Tea Company</a>, a U.S.-based supermarket chain</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/A%26W_Root_Beer" title="A&amp;W Root Beer">A&amp;W Root Beer</a> – named after founders Roy Allen and Frank Wright<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/A._Le_Coq" title="A. Le Coq">A. Le Coq</a> – named after the founder <a href="/wiki/Albert_von_Le_Coq" title="Albert von Le Coq"><b>A</b>lbert von <b>Le Coq</b></a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Abba_Seafood" title="Abba Seafood">Abba Seafood</a> – from <b>A</b>ktie<b>b</b>olaget <b>B</b>röderna <b>A</b>meln, meaning "Ameln brothers <a href="/wiki/Limited_company" title="Limited company">limited company</a>".</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">ABC</a> – American Broadcasting Company</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Abloy" class="mw-redirect" title="Abloy">Abloy</a> – derived from <i>Aktiebolag Låsfabriken Lukkotehdas Osakeyhtiö</i>, which means "lock factory <a href="/wiki/Limited_company" title="Limited company">limited company</a>" in both <a href="/wiki/Swedish_language" title="Swedish language">Swedish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Finnish_language" title="Finnish language">Finnish</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/ABN_AMRO" title="ABN AMRO">ABN AMRO</a> – in the 1960s, the <a href="/wiki/Nederlandsche_Handel-Maatschappij" class="mw-redirect" title="Nederlandsche Handel-Maatschappij">Nederlandsche Handel-Maatschappij</a> (Dutch Trading Society; 1824) and De Twentsche Bank merged to form the <a href="/wiki/Algemene_Bank_Nederland" title="Algemene Bank Nederland">Algemene Bank Nederland</a> (ABN; General Bank of the Netherlands); in 1966, the Amsterdamsche Bank and the Rotterdamsche Bank merged to form the <a href="/wiki/Amro_Bank" class="mw-redirect" title="Amro Bank">Amro Bank</a>; in 1991, ABN and Amro Bank merged to form ABN AMRO.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Accenture" title="Accenture">Accenture</a> – from "Accent on the future". The name Accenture was proposed by a company employee in Norway as part of an internal name finding process (<i>BrandStorming</i>). Before 1 January 2001, the company was called <a href="/wiki/Andersen_Consulting" class="mw-redirect" title="Andersen Consulting">Andersen Consulting</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Acer_Inc." title="Acer Inc.">Acer</a> – born as Multitech International in 1976, the company changed its name to Acer in 1987; the Latin word for “sharp, acute, able and facile”</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Adecco" class="mw-redirect" title="Adecco">Adecco</a> – named from the merger of Swiss staffing company Adia with French staffing company Ecco<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Adidas" title="Adidas">Adidas</a> – from the name of the founder Adolf (Adi) Dassler.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Adolf and his brother <a href="/wiki/Rudolf_Dassler" title="Rudolf Dassler">Rudolf Dassler</a> split the original company, <i>Gebrüder Dassler Schuhfabrik</i> (Dassler Brothers Shoe Factory), with Rudolf founding Puma.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Adobe_Systems" class="mw-redirect" title="Adobe Systems">Adobe Systems</a> – from the <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Creek_(near_Los_Altos,_California)" class="mw-redirect" title="Adobe Creek (near Los Altos, California)">Adobe Creek</a> that ran behind the house of co-founder <a href="/wiki/John_Warnock" title="John Warnock">John Warnock</a><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Aflac" title="Aflac">Aflac</a> – initialism for the company's previous name of American Family Life Assurance Company of Columbus (which remains the legal name of Aflac's underwriting subsidiary).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ahlstrom" class="mw-redirect" title="Ahlstrom">Ahlstrom</a> – named after founder <a href="/wiki/Antti_Ahlstr%C3%B6m" title="Antti Ahlström">Antti Ahlström</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ahold" title="Ahold">Ahold</a> – <a href="/wiki/Holding_company" title="Holding company">holding company</a> of <a href="/wiki/Albert_Heijn" title="Albert Heijn">Albert Heijn</a> and other supermarkets. For its 100th anniversary in 1987, Ahold was granted the title of <i>Koninklijke</i>  ("Royal" in <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>) by the <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_the_Netherlands" title="Monarchy of the Netherlands">Monarchy of the Netherlands</a>, changing its name to Koninklijke Ahold (Royal Ahold).<sup id="cite_ref-ROYAL-AHOLD-Apr-1999-20-F_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ROYAL-AHOLD-Apr-1999-20-F-16">[16]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Akai" title="Akai">Akai</a> – named for its founder, Masukichi Akai<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Akamai_Technologies" title="Akamai Technologies">Akamai</a> – from the <a href="/wiki/Hawaiian_language" title="Hawaiian language">Hawaiian</a> word akamai meaning smart or clever;<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> the company defines it as "intelligent, clever and cool"<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/AKG_Acoustics" class="mw-redirect" title="AKG Acoustics">AKG Acoustics</a> – from the company’s original name, Akustische und Kino-Geräte (Acoustic and Cinema Equipment)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/AkzoNobel" title="AkzoNobel">AKZO</a> – named from the 1969 merger of <a href="/wiki/Algemene_Kunstzijde_Unie" class="mw-redirect" title="Algemene Kunstzijde Unie">Algemene Kunstzijde Unie</a> (AKU) and Koninklijke Zout Organon (KZO)<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Alcatel-Lucent" title="Alcatel-Lucent">Alcatel-Lucent</a> – Alcatel was named from <b>Al</b>sacienne de <b>C</b>onstructions <b>At</b>omiques, de <b>T</b>élécommunications et d'<b>Él</b>ectronique.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> It took over Lucent Technologies (below) in 2006.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Alcoa" title="Alcoa">Alcoa</a> – Aluminum Company of America<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Aldi" title="Aldi">Aldi</a> – portmanteau of Albrecht (name of the founders) and discount</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Alfa_Romeo" title="Alfa Romeo">Alfa Romeo</a> – company was originally known as ALFA, an acronym for Anonima Lombarda Fabbrica Automobili. When Nicola Romeo bought ALFA in 1915, his surname was appended.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Alltel" title="Alltel">Alltel</a> – from original company name Allied Telephone Company</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Alps_Electric" title="Alps Electric">Alps Electric</a>/<a href="/wiki/Alpine_Electronics" title="Alpine Electronics">Alpine Electronics</a> – Katsutaro Kataoka founded Kataoka Electronics in a suburb of Tokyo in 1947. A subsidiary was established in the province of Tohoku, also known as the Tohoku Alps, as Tohoku Alps Co. Ltd. When Kataoka was seeking investment during the 1960s, he found that foreigners had difficulty pronouncing "Kataoka," and renamed his firm Alps Electric. Alpine Electronics was originally named Alps-<a href="/wiki/Motorola" title="Motorola">Motorola</a> as a joint venture in the Japanese car audio market and the Alpine name was adopted after Motorola divested its stake in 1978.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Alstom" title="Alstom">Alstom</a> – set up as Alsthom in 1928 by Société <b>Als</b>acienne de Constructions Mécaniques and Compagnie Française <b>Thom</b>son-Houston, it changed the spelling to Alstom in 1997.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/AltaVista" title="AltaVista">AltaVista</a> – Spanish for "high view"</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Alza" title="Alza">Alza</a> – from the name of the founder Alex Zaffaroni</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Amazon.com" class="mw-redirect" title="Amazon.com">Amazon.com</a> – founder <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Bezos" title="Jeff Bezos">Jeff Bezos</a> renamed the company "Amazon" (from the earlier name of Cadabra.com) after the world's most voluminous river, the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_River" title="Amazon River">Amazon</a>. He saw the potential for a larger volume of sales in an online (as opposed to a bricks and mortar) bookstore. (Alternative: Amazon was chosen to cash in on the popularity of Yahoo, which listed entries alphabetically.)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/AmBev" class="mw-redirect" title="AmBev">AmBev</a> – American Beverage Company, the largest Brazilian beverage company and fourth in the world. In 2004 it merged with <a href="/wiki/Interbrew" title="Interbrew">Interbrew</a> to create <a href="/wiki/InBev" title="InBev">InBev</a>, which in turn purchased <a href="/wiki/Anheuser-Busch" title="Anheuser-Busch">Anheuser-Busch</a> in 2008 to form <a href="/wiki/Anheuser-Busch_InBev" title="Anheuser-Busch InBev">Anheuser-Busch InBev</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/AMC_Theatres" title="AMC Theatres">AMC Theatres</a> – American Multi-Cinema: the company pioneered multi-screen cinemas<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Advanced_Micro_Devices" title="Advanced Micro Devices">AMD</a> – Advanced Micro Devices</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Amdahl_Corporation" title="Amdahl Corporation">Amdahl Corporation</a> – American mainframe computer company named after its founder, Dr. <a href="/wiki/Gene_Amdahl" title="Gene Amdahl">Gene Amdahl</a>, formerly of IBM. It was taken over by Fujitsu in 1997.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Amiga_Corporation" title="Amiga Corporation">Amiga Corporation</a> – original developers of the 16-bit <a href="/wiki/Amiga" title="Amiga">Amiga</a> computer chose the name, which means a 'female friend' in Spanish and Portuguese, because it sounded friendly, and because it came before rivals (<a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple Inc.</a> and <a href="/wiki/Atari" title="Atari">Atari</a>) alphabetically.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Amkor_Technology" title="Amkor Technology">AMKOR</a> – American Korea<b><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></b></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Amoco" title="Amoco">Amoco</a> – American Oil Company, now part of <a href="/wiki/BP" title="BP">BP</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Amstrad" title="Amstrad">Amstrad</a> – Amstrad Consumer Electronics plc was founded by Lord <a href="/wiki/Alan_Michael_Sugar" class="mw-redirect" title="Alan Michael Sugar">Alan Michael Sugar</a> in the UK. The name is a contraction of Alan Michael Sugar Trading.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Anheuser-Busch_InBev" title="Anheuser-Busch InBev">Anheuser-Busch InBev</a> – formed by the 2008 purchase of <a href="/wiki/Anheuser-Busch" title="Anheuser-Busch">Anheuser-Busch</a> by <a href="/wiki/InBev" title="InBev">InBev</a>. Anheuser-Busch was named for the company's original founder, <a href="/wiki/Eberhard_Anheuser" title="Eberhard Anheuser">Eberhard Anheuser</a>, and his later partner <a href="/wiki/Adolphus_Busch" title="Adolphus Busch">Adolphus Busch</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/AOL" title="AOL">AOL</a> – from America Online. The company was founded in 1983 as Quantum Computer Services.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Apache_Software_Foundation" class="mw-redirect" title="Apache Software Foundation">Apache</a> – according to the project's 1997 FAQ: "The Apache group was formed around a number of people who provided patch files that had been written for NCSA httpd 1.3. The result after combining them was A PAtCHy server."<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple</a> – for the favorite fruit of co-founder <a href="/wiki/Steve_Jobs" title="Steve Jobs">Steve Jobs</a> and/or for the time he worked at an apple orchard, and to distance itself from the cold, unapproachable, complicated imagery created by other computer companies at the time – which had names such as <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a>, <a href="/wiki/Digital_Equipment_Corporation" title="Digital Equipment Corporation">DEC</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cincom" class="mw-redirect" title="Cincom">Cincom</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Apricot_Computers" title="Apricot Computers">Apricot Computers</a> – early UK-based microcomputer company founded by ACT (Applied Computer Techniques), a business software and services supplier. The company wanted a "fruity" name (Apple and Acorn were popular brands) that included the letters A, C and T. Apricot fit the bill.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Arby%27s" title="Arby's">Arby's</a> – enunciation of the initials of its founders, the Raffel Brothers. The partners wanted to use the name Big Tex, but were unsuccessful in negotiating with the Akron businessman who was already using the name. So, Forrest said, "We came up with Arby's, which stands for R.B., the initials of Raffel Brothers, although I guess customers might think the initials stand for roast beef."</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Arcelor" title="Arcelor">Arcelor</a> – created in 2001 by a merger of <a href="/wiki/Arbed" class="mw-redirect" title="Arbed">Arbed</a> (Luxembourg), <a href="/wiki/Aceralia" title="Aceralia">Aceralia</a> (Spain) and <a href="/wiki/Usinor" title="Usinor">Usinor</a> (France) with the ambition of becoming a major player in the steel industry.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Grupo_Arcor" title="Grupo Arcor">Arcor</a> – Arroyito, Córdoba, the city where it was founded.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Areva" title="Areva">Areva</a> – named from the region of <a href="/wiki/%C3%81vila_(province)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ávila (province)">Ávila</a> in northern Spain, location of the Arevalo abbey. Arevalo was shorted to AREVA.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Aricent" title="Aricent">Aricent</a> – communications software company name created in 2006 by combining two words "arise" and "ascent".</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Arm_%26_Hammer_(brand)" class="mw-redirect" title="Arm &amp; Hammer (brand)">Arm &amp; Hammer</a> – based on the arm and hammer of Vulcan, the Roman god of fire and metalworking. It was previously the logo of the Vulcan Spice Mills in Brooklyn. When James Church, the son of Church &amp; Dwight founder Austin Church, came to Church and Dwight from Vulcan Spice Mills, he brought the logo with him.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/ARM_Limited" class="mw-redirect" title="ARM Limited">ARM Limited</a> – named after the microprocessor developed by small UK company Acorn as a successor to the 6502 used in its BBC Microcomputer. ARM originally stood for Acorn Risc Machine. When the company was spun off with backing from Apple and VTI, this was changed to Advanced Risc Machines.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/ARP_Instruments,_Inc." class="mw-redirect" title="ARP Instruments, Inc.">ARP</a> – company that made analog synthesizers in the 1970s, named after founder Alan Robert Pearlman</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Natura_Artis_Magistra" title="Natura Artis Magistra">Artis</a> – zoo in Amsterdam; named from the Latin phrase <i>Natura Artis Magistra</i>, or "Nature is Art's Teacher"</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Asda" title="Asda">Asda</a> – Asda Stores Limited was founded as Associated Dairies &amp; Farm Stores Ltd in 1949. However, the formation of the Asda name occurred in 1965 with the merger of the Asquith chain of three supermarkets and Associated Dairies; it is an abbreviation of Asquith and Dairies, a large UK supermarket chain that is now a subsidiary of <a href="/wiki/Walmart" title="Walmart">Walmart</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/ASICS" class="mw-redirect" title="ASICS">ASICS</a> – acronym for Anima Sana In Corpore Sano, which, translated from Latin, means "Healthy soul in a healthy body". Originally the citation is <i><a href="/wiki/List_of_Latin_phrases_(F%E2%80%93O)#M" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Latin phrases (F–O)">mens sana in corpore sano</a></i>, but MSICS does not sound as good.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ask.com" title="Ask.com">Ask.com</a> – search engine formerly named after <a href="/wiki/Jeeves" title="Jeeves">Jeeves</a>, the gentleman's gentleman (<a href="/wiki/Valet" title="Valet">valet</a>, <i>not</i> <a href="/wiki/Butler" title="Butler">butler</a>) in <a href="/wiki/P._G._Wodehouse" title="P. G. Wodehouse">P. G. Wodehouse</a>'s series of books. Ask Jeeves was shortened to Ask in 2006.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Aston_Martin" title="Aston Martin">Aston Martin</a> – from the "Aston Hill" races (near <a href="/wiki/Aston_Clinton" title="Aston Clinton">Aston Clinton</a>) where the company was founded, and the surname of <a href="/wiki/Lionel_Martin" title="Lionel Martin">Lionel Martin</a>, the company's founder.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Asus" title="Asus">Asus</a> – named after <a href="/wiki/Pegasus" title="Pegasus">Pegasus</a>, the winged horse of Greek mythology. The first three letters of the word were dropped to get a high position in alphabetical listings. An Asus company named Pegatron, using the spare letters, was spun off in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/AT%26T" title="AT&amp;T">AT&amp;T</a> – American Telephone and Telegraph Corporation officially changed its name to AT&amp;T in the 1990s.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Atari" title="Atari">Atari</a> – named from the board game <a href="/wiki/Go_(board_game)" class="mw-redirect" title="Go (board game)">Go</a>. "Atari" is a Japanese word to describe a position where an opponent's stones are in danger of being captured. It is similar, though not identical, to "check" in chess. The original games company was American but wanted a Japanese-sounding name.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/ATI_Technologies" title="ATI Technologies">ATI Technologies</a> – founded in Canada as <b>A</b>rray <b>T</b>echnology <b>I</b>nc. and taken over by AMD in 2006.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/ATS_(wheels)" title="ATS (wheels)">ATS</a> – Auto Technik Spezialerzeugnisse, a German company producing light alloy wheels and motor parts, which ran its own Formula 1 racing team in the late 1970s and early 1980s.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Audi" title="Audi">Audi</a> – Latin translation of the German name "Horch". The founder <a href="/wiki/August_Horch" title="August Horch">August Horch</a> left the company after five years, but still wanted to manufacture cars. Since the original "Horch" company was still there, he called his new company Audi, the Latin form of his last name. In English it is "hark".</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="B">B</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_company_name_etymologies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: B">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/B%26H_Photo_Video" class="mw-redirect" title="B&amp;H Photo Video">B&amp;H Photo Video</a> – named after <b>B</b>limie Schreiber and her husband, company founder <b>H</b>erman Schreiber</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/B%26Q" title="B&amp;Q">B&amp;Q</a> – from the initials of its founders, Richard <b>B</b>lock and David <b>Q</b>uayle</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Babolat" title="Babolat">Babolat</a> – racquet sports (tennis, badminton, squash) equipment company named after its founder, Pierre Babolat</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bahco" title="Bahco">Bahco</a> – from the name B.A. Hjort &amp; Company. Founder Berndt August Hjort signed a deal to distribute the tools of inventor <a href="/wiki/Johan_Petter_Johansson" title="Johan Petter Johansson">Johan Petter Johansson</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bakkav%C3%B6r" title="Bakkavör">Bakkavör</a> – from the street in a <a href="/wiki/Reykjav%C3%ADk" title="Reykjavík">Reykjavík</a> suburb where the founders grew up<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bally_Manufacturing" title="Bally Manufacturing">Bally</a> – originally Lion Manufacturing, the company changed its name to Bally after the success of its first popular pinball machine, <i>Ballyhoo</i>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Banesto" title="Banesto">Banesto</a> – from <b>Ban</b>co <b>Es</b>pañol de Crédi<b>to</b> (<i>Spanish Credit Bank</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bang_%26_Olufsen" title="Bang &amp; Olufsen">Bang &amp; Olufsen</a> – from the names of its founders, Peter <b>Bang</b> and Svend <b>Olufsen</b>, who met at a school of engineering in Denmark.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/A_Bathing_Ape" title="A Bathing Ape">BAPE</a> – A <b>B</b>athing <b>Ape</b> is a cult clothing company founded by <a href="/wiki/Nigo" title="Nigo">Tomoaki "Nigo" Nagao</a> in 1993.<sup id="cite_ref-TheHipHopIcon_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TheHipHopIcon-30">[30]</a></sup> The name is derived from a Japanese saying, "A Bathing Ape in Lukewarm Water", which Nigo says is "a reference to the young generation being spoiled, pampered and too complacent."<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/BASF" title="BASF">BASF</a> – from <b>B</b>adische <b>A</b>nilin und <b>S</b>oda <b>F</b>abriken. Anilin and soda were the first products. "Badisch" refers to the location in the state of Baden, Germany (Black Forest region).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bauhaus_(company)" title="Bauhaus (company)">Bauhaus</a> – European chain of DIY stores founded by <a href="/wiki/Heinz-Georg_Baus" title="Heinz-Georg Baus">Heinz-Georg Baus</a> and named from the <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a> words <i>bauen</i> (to build) and <i>Haus</i> (house). The reference to the classic <a href="/wiki/Bauhaus" title="Bauhaus">Bauhaus</a> art school is only an allusion.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bauknecht_(company)" title="Bauknecht (company)">Bauknecht</a> – founded as an electrotechnical <a href="/wiki/Workshop" title="Workshop">workshop</a> in 1919 by <a href="/wiki/Gottlob_Bauknecht" title="Gottlob Bauknecht">Gottlob Bauknecht</a>, and now a <a href="/wiki/Whirlpool" title="Whirlpool">Whirlpool</a> brand</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bayer" title="Bayer">Bayer</a> – named after Friedrich Bayer, who founded the company in 1863</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> – <b>B</b>ritish <b>B</b>roadcasting <b>C</b>orporation, originally <a href="/wiki/British_Broadcasting_Company" title="British Broadcasting Company">British Broadcasting Company</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Banco_Bilbao_Vizcaya_Argentaria" title="Banco Bilbao Vizcaya Argentaria">BBVA</a> – <b>B</b>anco <b>B</b>ilbao <b>V</b>izcaya <b>A</b>rgentaria, a Spanish banking group formed in 1999 from the merger of Banco Bilbao Vizcaya and Argentaria</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/BEA_Systems" title="BEA Systems">BEA Systems</a> – from the first initial of each of the company's three founders: <b>B</b>ill Coleman, <b>E</b>d Scott and <b>A</b>lfred Chuang</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Beko" title="Beko">Beko</a> – Turkish consumer electronics company named after its founders, <b>Be</b>jerano and <b>Ko</b>ç<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ben_%26_Jerry%27s" title="Ben &amp; Jerry's">Ben &amp; Jerry's</a> – named after <b>Ben</b> Cohen and <b>Jerry</b> Greenfield, who founded an ice cream parlor in 1978 after completing a correspondence course on ice cream making from Pennsylvania State University. The company, Ben &amp; Jerry's Homemade Holdings, Inc. was later taken over by <a href="/wiki/Unilever" title="Unilever">Unilever</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/BenQ" title="BenQ">BenQ</a> – <b>B</b>ringing <b>En</b>joyment and <b>Q</b>uality to life<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Berkshire_Hathaway" title="Berkshire Hathaway">Berkshire Hathaway</a> – originally a textile company formed by the merger of <a href="/wiki/Berkshire_Fine_Spinning_Associates" title="Berkshire Fine Spinning Associates">Berkshire Fine Spinning Associates</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Hathaway_Manufacturing_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Hathaway Manufacturing Company">Hathaway Manufacturing Company</a>. In 1964, the declining company was taken over by one of its investors, <a href="/wiki/Warren_Buffett" title="Warren Buffett">Warren Buffett</a>, who converted it into a conglomerate holding company.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/BHP" title="BHP">BHP</a> – <b>B</b>roken <b>H</b>ill <b>P</b>roprietary, named after the town of <a href="/wiki/Broken_Hill" title="Broken Hill">Broken Hill</a>, where BHP was founded</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Soci%C3%A9t%C3%A9_Bic" title="Société Bic">BIC Corporation</a> – pen company was named after one of its founders, Marcel Bich. He dropped the final <i>h</i> to avoid a potentially inappropriate English pronunciation of the name.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Black_%26_Decker" title="Black &amp; Decker">Black &amp; Decker</a> – named after founders S. Duncan Black and Alonzo G. Decker.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/BlackBerry_Limited" title="BlackBerry Limited">BlackBerry</a> – first device produced by the company originally known as Research In Motion (below) was a two-way pager; the BlackBerry name was chosen because of the resemblance between the keyboard buttons and the drupelets that form the blackberry fruit. The company rebranded itself as BlackBerry in 2013.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Blaupunkt" title="Blaupunkt">Blaupunkt</a> – Blaupunkt ("Blue dot") was founded in 1923 under the name "Ideal". Its core business was the manufacturing of <a href="/wiki/Headphone" class="mw-redirect" title="Headphone">headphones</a>. If the headphones came through quality tests, the company would give the headphones a blue dot. The headphones quickly became known as the <i>blue dots</i> or <i>blaue Punkte</i>. The quality symbol would become a trademark and the trademark would become the company name in 1938.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Blizzard_Entertainment" title="Blizzard Entertainment">Blizzard Entertainment</a> - videogame company founded in 1991 as Silicon &amp; Synapse, it briefly changed its name to Chaos Studios (1993–94),<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> before discovering there was already a company using the Chaos name. It picked Blizzard from the dictionary.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/BMW" title="BMW">BMW</a> – <b>B</b>ayerische <b>M</b>otoren <b>W</b>erke (<i>Bavarian Motor Works</i>).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bo-Dyn_Bobsled_Project" title="Bo-Dyn Bobsled Project">Bo-Dyn Bobsled Project</a> – <a href="/wiki/Geoff_Bodine" title="Geoff Bodine">Geoff <b>Bo</b>dine</a> and Chassis <b>Dyn</b>amics, the bobsled maker that the <a href="/wiki/NASCAR" title="NASCAR">NASCAR</a> driver teamed with. The company name is pronounced the same as that of Bodine himself: <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/oʊ/: 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span><span title="/aɪ/: 'i' in 'tide'">aɪ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span></span>/</a></span></span>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Boeing" title="Boeing">Boeing</a> – named after founder William E. Boeing. It was originally called Pacific Aero Products Co.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Robert_Bosch_GmbH" title="Robert Bosch GmbH">Bosch</a> – named after founder Robert Bosch. <i>Robert Bosch GmbH</i> (full company name) is a German diversified technology-based corporation.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bose_Corporation" title="Bose Corporation">Bose Corporation</a> – named after founder <a href="/wiki/Amar_Bose" title="Amar Bose">Amar Bose</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/BP" title="BP">BP</a> – formerly <b>B</b>ritish <b>P</b>etroleum, now BP (The slogan "Beyond Petroleum" has incorrectly been taken to refer to the company's new name following its rebranding effort in 2000.)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/BRAC_(organization)" title="BRAC (organization)">BRAC</a> – <b>B</b>angladesh <b>R</b>ural &amp; <b>A</b>dvancement <b>C</b>ommittee, world's largest NGO (non-governmental organization)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bridgestone" title="Bridgestone">Bridgestone</a> – named after founder Shojiro Ishibashi. The surname <i>Ishibashi</i> (石橋) means "stone bridge", or "bridge of stone".</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Brine,_Corp." class="mw-redirect" title="Brine, Corp.">Brine, Corp.</a> – sporting goods company named after founder, W.H. Brine. It was taken over by <a href="/wiki/New_Balance" title="New Balance">New Balance</a> in 2006.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Brooks_Sports" title="Brooks Sports">Brooks Sports</a> – anglicized version of Bruchs, the maiden name of the wife of founder Morris Goldenberg.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Brunswick_Corporation" title="Brunswick Corporation">Brunswick Corporation</a> – founded in 1845 as "J.M. Brunswick Manufacturing Company" in Cincinnati, Ohio by John Moses Brunswick, an immigrant from Bremgarten, Switzerland</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Birmingham_Small_Arms_Company" title="Birmingham Small Arms Company">BSA</a> – <b>B</b>irmingham <b>S</b>mall <b>A</b>rms Company, which started out making guns but later became best known for its motorcycles.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/BT_Group" title="BT Group">BT</a> – formerly <b>B</b>ritish <b>T</b>elecom (from BT Group, formerly British Telecommunications plc.)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Buick" title="Buick">Buick</a> – named for its founder, <a href="/wiki/David_Dunbar_Buick" title="David Dunbar Buick">David Dunbar Buick</a>. The company was the original focal point for <a href="/wiki/General_Motors" title="General Motors">General Motors</a>, established in 1908 as a holding company for Buick plus other companies acquired by <a href="/wiki/William_C._Durant" title="William C. Durant">William C. Durant</a>. Buick survives to this day as a GM brand.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Groupe_Bull" title="Groupe Bull">Bull</a> – <i>Compagnie des machines Bull</i> was founded in Paris to exploit the patents for punched card machines taken out by Norwegian engineer <a href="/wiki/Fredrik_Rosing_Bull" title="Fredrik Rosing Bull">Fredrik Rosing Bull</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Burroughs_Corporation" title="Burroughs Corporation">Burroughs Corporation</a> – founded in 1886 as the American Arithmometer Company and later renamed after the adding machine invented by <a href="/wiki/William_Seward_Burroughs_I" title="William Seward Burroughs I">William Seward Burroughs</a>. The company took over <a href="/wiki/Sperry_Corporation" title="Sperry Corporation">Sperry Corporation</a> and became <a href="/wiki/Unisys" title="Unisys">Unisys</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bultaco" title="Bultaco">Bultaco</a> – Spanish company of motorcycles, which disappeared in the 1980s. Its name is based on the name of its founder, P<b>aco</b> <b>Bult</b>ó.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/ByWater_Solutions" title="ByWater Solutions">ByWater Solutions</a> – library software company named after a village in <a href="/wiki/J._R._R._Tolkien" title="J. R. R. Tolkien">J. R. R. Tolkien</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings" title="The Lord of the Rings">The Lord of the Rings</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="C">C</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_company_name_etymologies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: C">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/C%26A" title="C&amp;A">C&amp;A</a> – named after the brothers <b>C</b>lemens and <b>A</b>ugust Brenninkmeijer, who founded a textile company called C&amp;A in the Netherlands in 1841</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/CA,_Inc." class="mw-redirect" title="CA, Inc.">CA</a>  – <b>C</b>omputer <b>A</b>ssociates was founded in 1976 as Computer Associates International, Inc. by <a href="/wiki/Charles_Wang" title="Charles Wang">Charles Wang</a> and <a href="/wiki/Russell_Artzt" title="Russell Artzt">Russell Artzt</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cadillac" title="Cadillac">Cadillac</a> – the car company, founded in 1902, was named after the 18th-century French explorer <a href="/wiki/Antoine_Laumet_de_La_Mothe,_sieur_de_Cadillac" class="mw-redirect" title="Antoine Laumet de La Mothe, sieur de Cadillac">Antoine Laumet de La Mothe, sieur de Cadillac</a>. <a href="/wiki/Cadillac,_Gironde" title="Cadillac, Gironde">Cadillac</a> is a small town in the <a href="/wiki/Southern_France" title="Southern France">South of France</a>. The company was taken over by General Motors in 1909 and survives as a GM brand.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/CAE_(company)" class="mw-redirect" title="CAE (company)">CAE</a> – originally <b>C</b>anadian <b>A</b>viation <b>E</b>lectronics</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Campagnolo" title="Campagnolo">Campagnolo</a> – from the name of its founder, <a href="/wiki/Tullio_Campagnolo" title="Tullio Campagnolo">Tullio Campagnolo</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Canon_(company)" class="mw-redirect" title="Canon (company)">Canon</a> – originally (1933) "Precision Optical Instruments Laboratory", the new name (1935) derived from the name of the company's first camera, the <a href="/wiki/Kwanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Kwanon">Kwanon</a>, in turn named after the Japanese name of the Buddhist <a href="/wiki/Bodhisattva" title="Bodhisattva">bodhisattva</a> of mercy.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Capcom" title="Capcom">Capcom</a> – <b>Cap</b>sule <b>Com</b>puters, the former name of the company and how they described the arcade machines they manufactured at the time</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Caprabo" title="Caprabo">Caprabo</a> – Catalan supermarkets, founded by Pere <b>Ca</b>rbó, Jaume <b>Pra</b>ts and Josep <b>Bo</b>net</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Carrefour" title="Carrefour">Carrefour</a> – chain of supermarkets and hypermarkets which started with a store near a crossroads (carrefour in French) in Annecy</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Casio" title="Casio">Casio</a> – from the name of its founder, Kashio Tadao, who had set up the company Kashio Seisakujo as a subcontractor factory</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Caterpillar_Inc." title="Caterpillar Inc.">Caterpillar</a> – originally Holt Tractor Co, merged with Best Tractor Co. in 1925. A company photographer exclaimed aloud of a Holt tractor that the tracks' movement resembled a caterpillar moving along the ground. The name stuck.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cathay_Pacific_Airways_Limited" class="mw-redirect" title="Cathay Pacific Airways Limited">Cathay Pacific Airways Limited</a> – airline was founded on 24 September 1946 by American Roy C. Farrell and Australian Sydney H. de Kantzow, with each man putting up HK$1 to register the airline. They named it Cathay Pacific because Cathay was the ancient name given to China; and Pacific because Farrell speculated that they would one day fly across the Pacific.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">CBS</a> – <b>C</b>olumbia <b>B</b>roadcasting <b>S</b>ystem</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Celera_Corporation" title="Celera Corporation">Celera</a> – inspired by ‘celerity’ or swiftness (in decoding the human genome),<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> with "era of the cell" a secondary meaning<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cemex" title="Cemex">Cemex</a> – portmanteau of the company's former name of <i><b>Ce</b>mentos <b>Mex</b>icanos</i> (Spanish for "Mexican Cement")</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cerner" title="Cerner">Cerner</a> – from the Latin "cerner" meaning "to discern"<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/CGI_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="CGI Group">CGI Group</a> – from the first letters of Information Management Consultant in French (<b>C</b>onseillers en <b>G</b>estion et <b>I</b>nformatique)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chello" title="Chello">Chello</a> – Dutch internet service provider, its name was originally pronounced 'say hello' (in Dutch the letter C at the beginning of a word is pronounced 'say'). This did not catch on and now it is pronounced "cello" (as in the stringed instrument).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chevrolet" title="Chevrolet">Chevrolet</a> – named after company co-founder <a href="/wiki/Louis_Chevrolet" title="Louis Chevrolet">Louis Chevrolet</a>, a Swiss-born auto racer. The company was merged into General Motors in 1917 and survives only as a brand name.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chrysler" title="Chrysler">Chrysler</a> – named after the company founder, <a href="/wiki/Walter_P._Chrysler" class="mw-redirect" title="Walter P. Chrysler">Walter P. Chrysler</a>. Merged with <a href="/wiki/Fiat_S.p.A." title="Fiat S.p.A.">Fiat</a> in 2014 to create <a href="/wiki/Fiat_Chrysler_Automobiles" title="Fiat Chrysler Automobiles">Fiat Chrysler Automobiles</a> (FCA), with the Chrysler corporate entity becoming the Fiat Chrysler subsidiary FCA US. The "Chrysler" name survives as a <a href="/wiki/Chrysler_(brand)" class="mw-redirect" title="Chrysler (brand)">brand</a> of FCA US.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Novartis" title="Novartis">Ciba Geigy</a> – CIBA, named from <b>C</b>hemical <b>I</b>ndustry <b>Ba</b>sel (after <a href="/wiki/Basel" title="Basel">Basel</a> in Switzerland), merged with a company named after its founder Johann Rudolf <b>Geigy</b>-Merian. It became <a href="/wiki/Novartis" title="Novartis">Novartis</a> (below) after a merger with <a href="/wiki/Sandoz" class="mw-redirect" title="Sandoz">Sandoz</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/CiCi%27s_Pizza" class="mw-redirect" title="CiCi's Pizza">CiCi's Pizza</a> – from the first letters of the last names of the founders of the franchise (Joe <b>C</b>roce and Mike <b>C</b>ole)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cigna" title="Cigna">Cigna</a> – CIGNA was formed in 1982 through the combination of <b>I</b>nsurance Company of <b>N</b>orth <b>A</b>merica (INA) and <b>C</b>onnecticut <b>G</b>eneral (CG). The name is a combination of the letters of the predecessor companies, CG and INA.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cincom" class="mw-redirect" title="Cincom">Cincom</a> – originally called United Computer Systems, which was similar to several other software and services companies of the day. Two of the three founders visited Philco (Philadelphia Company), and this inspired them to create a new company name derived from <b>Cin</b>cinnati (where it was based) and <b>Com</b>puter (its business).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cisco_Systems" title="Cisco Systems">Cisco</a> – short for San Fran<b>cisco</b>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Citro%C3%ABn" title="Citroën">Citroën</a> – named after <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_Citro%C3%ABn" title="André Citroën">André Citroën</a> (1878–1935), a French entrepreneur of Dutch descent. He was the fifth and last child of the Dutch Jewish diamond merchant Levie Citroen and Mazra Kleinmann (of Warsaw, Poland). The Citroen family moved to Paris from Amsterdam in 1873 where the name changed to Citroën.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/CKX,_Inc." class="mw-redirect" title="CKX, Inc.">CKX, Inc.</a> – named from "<b>C</b>ontent is <b>K</b>ing", with the <b>X</b> from founder <a href="/wiki/Robert_F.X._Sillerman" class="mw-redirect" title="Robert F.X. Sillerman">Robert F.X. Sillerman</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> Other Sillerman companies include SFX Entertainment and FXM Asset Management.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Clarion_(car_audio)" class="mw-redirect" title="Clarion (car audio)">Clarion</a> – named after the "bugle-like wind instrument used in ancient Greece", says the company, which wanted a name English speakers would find easy to remember. It was founded in Japan in 1940 as Hakusan Wireless Electric Company, making radios, and became Teikoku Dempa after merging with Takizawa Wireless Electric Industries in 1943.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">CNN</a> – <b>C</b>able <b>N</b>ews <b>N</b>etwork</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola" title="Coca-Cola">Coca-Cola</a> – derived from the <a href="/wiki/Coca" title="Coca">coca leaves</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kola_nut" title="Kola nut">kola nuts</a> used as flavoring. Coca-Cola creator <a href="/wiki/John_S._Pemberton" class="mw-redirect" title="John S. Pemberton">John S. Pemberton</a> changed the 'K' of kola to 'C' to make the name look better.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Coleco" title="Coleco">Coleco</a> – began as the <b>Co</b>nnecticut <b>Le</b>ather <b>Co</b>mpany</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Colgate-Palmolive" title="Colgate-Palmolive">Colgate-Palmolive</a> – formed from a merger of soap manufacturers Colgate &amp; Company and Palmolive-Peet. <i>Peet</i> was dropped in 1953. <i>Colgate</i> was named after William Colgate, an English immigrant, who set up a starch, soap and candle business in New York City in 1806. <i>Palmolive</i> was named for the two oils (Palm and Olive) used in its manufacture.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/COLT_Telecom_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="COLT Telecom Group">COLT</a> – from <b>C</b>ity <b>O</b>f <b>L</b>ondon <b>T</b>elecom</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Comcast" title="Comcast">Comcast</a> – from <b>com</b>munications and broad<b>cast</b></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Commodore_International" title="Commodore International">Commodore International</a> – supposedly named after the <a href="/wiki/Opel_Commodore" title="Opel Commodore">Opel Commodore</a>, after the company's founder <a href="/wiki/Jack_Tramiel" title="Jack Tramiel">Jack Tramiel</a> had unsuccessfully tried to name his company first "General" and then "Admiral".<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> However, the Opel Commodore only debuted in 1967, years after the company's founding.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Compaq" title="Compaq">Compaq</a> – from <b>comp</b>uter and "pack" to denote a small integral object; or: Compatibility And Quality; or: from the company's first product, the very <i>compact</i> <a href="/wiki/Compaq_Portable" title="Compaq Portable">Compaq Portable</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/COMSAT" title="COMSAT">COMSAT</a> – contraction of <b>com</b>munications <b>sat</b>ellites. This American digital telecommunications and <a href="/wiki/Satellite" title="Satellite">satellite</a> company was founded during the era of U.S. President <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a> era to develop the technology.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/ConocoPhillips" title="ConocoPhillips">ConocoPhillips</a> – formed from the merger of <a href="/wiki/Conoco" title="Conoco">Conoco</a> (from <b>Con</b>tinental <b>O</b>il <b>Co</b>mpany) and the <a href="/wiki/Phillips_Petroleum_Company" title="Phillips Petroleum Company">Phillips Petroleum Company</a>, named after the brothers who founded it: Lee Eldas "L.E." and <a href="/wiki/Frank_Phillips_(oil_industrialist)" title="Frank Phillips (oil industrialist)">Frank Phillips</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Copersucar" title="Copersucar">Copersucar</a> – <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazilian</a> production <a href="/wiki/Cooperative" title="Cooperative">cooperative</a> in sugar and alcohol; its name is a contraction of Cooperativa de Açucar e Álcool</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Corel_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Corel Corporation">Corel</a> – from <b>Co</b>wpland <b>Re</b>search <b>L</b>aboratory, after the name of the company's founder, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Cowpland" title="Michael Cowpland">Michael Cowpland</a><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cosworth" title="Cosworth">Cosworth</a> – automotive engineering company named after company founders Mike <b>Cos</b>tin and Keith Duck<b>worth</b>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Companhia_Paulista_de_For%C3%A7a_e_Luz" class="mw-redirect" title="Companhia Paulista de Força e Luz">CPFL</a> – Companhia Paulista de Força e Luz (<a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="São Paulo">São Paulo</a> Company of Light and Power), one of the largest in Brazil, based in <a href="/wiki/Campinas" title="Campinas">Campinas</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Crabtree_%26_Evelyn" title="Crabtree &amp; Evelyn">Crabtree &amp; Evelyn</a> – toiletry company named after gardener <a href="/wiki/John_Evelyn" title="John Evelyn">John Evelyn</a>, and the tree that bears <a href="/wiki/Crabapple" class="mw-redirect" title="Crabapple">Crabapples</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cray" title="Cray">Cray</a> – supercomputer company named after its founder, <a href="/wiki/Seymour_Cray" title="Seymour Cray">Seymour Cray</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/CRC_Press" title="CRC Press">CRC Press</a> – originally <b>C</b>hemical <b>R</b>ubber <b>C</b>ompany</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cromemco" title="Cromemco">Cromemco</a> – early microcomputer company in Silicon Valley (circa 1975–198?) founded by two PhD students who once lived at Stanford University's <b>Cro</b>thers <b>Mem</b>orial Hall (a dormitory)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cutco" title="Cutco">Cutco</a> – <b>C</b>ooking <b>Ut</b>ensils <b>Co</b>mpany<sup id="cite_ref-Cutco_history_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cutco_history-44">[44]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/CVS/pharmacy" class="mw-redirect" title="CVS/pharmacy">CVS</a> – originally <b>C</b>onsumer <b>V</b>alue <b>S</b>tores. CEO Tom Ryan has said he now considers "CVS" to stand for "Customer, Value, and Service".</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="D">D</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_company_name_etymologies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: D">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Daewoo" title="Daewoo">Daewoo</a> – company founder Kim Woo Chong called it Daewoo which means "Great House" or "Great Universe" in <a href="/wiki/Korean_language" title="Korean language">Korean</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/DAF_Trucks" title="DAF Trucks">DAF Trucks</a> – from 1932 the company's name was <i>Van <b>D</b>oorne's <b>A</b>anhangwagen <b>F</b>abriek</i> (Van Doorne's Trailer Factory). In 1949 the company started making trucks, trailers and buses and changed the name into <i>Van <b>D</b>oorne's <b>A</b>utomobiel <b>F</b>abriek</i> (Van Doorne's Automobile Factory).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Daihatsu" title="Daihatsu">Daihatsu</a> – first <a href="/wiki/Kanji" title="Kanji">kanji</a> from "Osaka" (大坂, the kanji is here pronounced <i>dai</i>) and "engine" (発動機, the first kanji is <i>hatsu</i>). Engine manufacturers were listed on the Tokyo and Osaka Stock Exchanges, and their names shortened to the first kanji. (The company listed on the Tokyo exchange is <a href="/wiki/Tohatsu" title="Tohatsu">Tohatsu</a>.)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Groupe_Danone" class="mw-redirect" title="Groupe Danone">Danone</a> (Dannon in the U.S.) – Isaac Carasso in Barcelona made his first yogurts with the nickname of his first son Daniel (DAN-ONE)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dassault_Aviation" title="Dassault Aviation">Dassault Aviation</a> – origins of the company go back to 1929 with SAAMB (<a href="/wiki/Soci%C3%A9t%C3%A9_des_Avions_Marcel_Bloch" title="Société des Avions Marcel Bloch">Société des Avions Marcel Bloch</a>), named after its founder Marcel Bloch (1892-1986). Bloch changed his name to <a href="/wiki/Marcel_Dassault" title="Marcel Dassault">Marcel Dassault</a> in 1949. Dassault was derived from <i>char d'assaut</i> (French for "assault wagon" or battle tank), the codename that his brother had used in the French resistance.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Datsun" title="Datsun">Datsun</a> – first called DAT, from the initials of its financiers Den, Aoyama and Takeuchi. Soon changed to DATSON to imply a smaller version of their original car, then (as SON can mean "loss" in Japanese) again to DATSUN when they were acquired by Nissan.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Digital_Equipment_Corporation" title="Digital Equipment Corporation">DEC</a> – <b>D</b>igital <b>E</b>quipment <b>C</b>orporation, a pioneering American minicomputer manufacturer founded by <a href="/wiki/Ken_Olsen" title="Ken Olsen">Ken Olsen</a> and taken over by Compaq, before Compaq was merged into Hewlett-Packard (HP). It was generally called DEC ("deck"), but later tried to rebrand itself as Digital.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/DEKA_(company)" title="DEKA (company)">DEKA</a> – named after its founder <b>De</b>an <b>Ka</b>men, developer of the Segway, iBOT, HomeChoice Dialysis and other products.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Delhaize_Group" title="Delhaize Group">Delhaize</a> – named after its founders, Jules Delhaize and his brothers, who originated from Charleroi (Belgium). They opened the first European self-service "supermarket" in Ixelles/Elsene, a Brussels borough.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dell" title="Dell">Dell</a> – named after its founder, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Dell" title="Michael Dell">Michael Dell</a>. The company changed its name from Dell Computer in 2003.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Denning_%26_Fourcade,_Inc." title="Denning &amp; Fourcade, Inc.">Denning &amp; Fourcade, Inc.</a> – interior designer company named after its founders <a href="/wiki/Robert_Denning" title="Robert Denning">Robert Denning</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vincent_Fourcade" title="Vincent Fourcade">Vincent Fourcade</a> in 1960.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/DHL_Express" class="mw-redirect" title="DHL Express">DHL</a> – named after its founders, Adrian <b>D</b>alsey, Larry <b>H</b>illblom, and Robert <b>L</b>ynn. DHL was taken over by the German post office and both now operate under the group name <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Post" title="Deutsche Post">Deutsche Post</a> DHL.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Diageo" title="Diageo">Diageo</a> – name created by branding consultancy <a href="/wiki/Wolff_Olins" title="Wolff Olins">Wolff Olins</a> in 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-diageowo_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diageowo-46">[46]</a></sup> It is based on the <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> word <i>diēs</i>, meaning "day", and the <a href="/wiki/Greek_root" class="mw-redirect" title="Greek root">Greek root</a> <i>geo-</i>, meaning "world". This refers to the company slogan, "Celebrating Life, Every Day, Everywhere".<sup id="cite_ref-diageowo_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diageowo-46">[46]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dick%27s_Sporting_Goods" title="Dick's Sporting Goods">Dick's Sporting Goods</a> – named after its founder, Dick Stack, who opened a bait and tackle shop in 1948 with a $300 gift from his grandmother<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Digg" title="Digg">Digg, Inc.</a> – Kevin Rose's friend David Prager (The Screen Savers, This Week in Tech) originally wanted to call the site "Diggnation", but Kevin wanted a simpler name. He chose the name "Digg", because users are able to "dig" stories, out of those submitted, up to the front page. The site was called "Digg" instead of "Dig" because the domain name "dig.com" was previously registered, by Walt Disney Internet Group. "Diggnation" would eventually be used as the title of Kevin Rose and Alex Albrecht's weekly podcast discussing popular stories from Digg.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Digi-Key" title="Digi-Key">Digi-Key</a> – electronic component distributor whose name is derived from founder <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Stordahl" title="Ronald Stordahl">Dr. Ronald Stordahl's</a> amateur radio telegraphic keyer, the "IC Keyer Kit", which utilized digital integrated circuits</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dillard%27s" title="Dillard's">Dillard's</a> – named for William T. Dillard who founded the Arkansas-based department store in 1938</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/DSG_International_(retailer)" class="mw-redirect" title="DSG International (retailer)">Dixons</a> – commonly used abbreviation for DSG International plc (<b>D</b>ixons <b>S</b>tores <b>G</b>roup), a UK-based retailer. The company was founded in 1937 by Charles Kalms and Michael Mindel. When opening their first photographic shop in Southend, they only had room for six letters on the fascia, and chose the name Dixons from the phone book.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/DKNY" title="DKNY">DKNY</a> – <b>D</b>onna <b>K</b>aran <b>N</b>ew <b>Y</b>ork</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Double_Fine_Productions" class="mw-redirect" title="Double Fine Productions">Double Fine Productions</a> – named after a sign upon the Golden Gate Bridge that warned patrons that it was "Double Fine Zone" referring to the fact that speeders would be charged twice.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dow_Chemical_Company" title="Dow Chemical Company">Dow</a> – named after its founder, <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Henry_Dow" title="Herbert Henry Dow">Herbert Henry Dow</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/DSM_(company)" title="DSM (company)">DSM</a> – established in 1902 to exploit the Dutch coal mines, the name meaning <b>D</b>utch <b>S</b>tate <b>M</b>ines. The last mine closed in 1973, and the company switched to chemicals.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Duane_Reade" title="Duane Reade">Duane Reade</a> – named after Duane and Reade Streets in lower Manhattan, where the chain's first warehouse was located.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> The chain was purchased by <a href="/wiki/Walgreens" title="Walgreens">Walgreens</a> in 2010, but still operates separately.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/DuPont" title="DuPont">DuPont</a> – short name for E. I. du Pont de Nemours and Company. This American chemical company was founded in 1802 as a gunpowder mill by <a href="/wiki/Eleuth%C3%A8re_Ir%C3%A9n%C3%A9e_du_Pont" class="mw-redirect" title="Eleuthère Irénée du Pont">Eleuthère Irénée du Pont</a>, who left France to escape the French Revolution.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dynegy" title="Dynegy">Dynegy</a> – Natural Gas Clearinghouse changed its name in 1998 to reflect its self-described traits as a <i>dynamic energy</i> company. "Dynergy" had already been taken by a German health foods company.</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="E">E</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_company_name_etymologies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: E">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/E._J._Korvette" title="E. J. Korvette">E. J. Korvette</a> – named for the founder <b>E</b>ugene Ferkauf and his associate <b>J</b>oe Swillenberg; an intentional misspelling of "<a href="/wiki/Corvette" title="Corvette">Corvette</a>". A common urban legend misstates the origin as "Eight Jewish Korean War Veterans".<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Electronic_Arts" title="Electronic Arts">EA</a> - <b>E</b>lectronic <b>A</b>rts. The company was founded in May 1982 as Amazin' Software and rebranded as Electronic Arts in October the same year.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/EBay" title="EBay">eBay</a> – Pierre Omidyar, who had created the Auction Web trading website, had formed a web consulting concern called Echo Bay Technology Group. "Echo Bay" did not refer to the town in Nevada, "It just sounded cool", Omidyar reportedly said. <a href="/wiki/Echo_Bay_Mines_Limited" class="mw-redirect" title="Echo Bay Mines Limited">Echo Bay Mines Limited</a>, a gold mining company, had already taken EchoBay.com, so Omidyar registered what (at the time) he thought was the second best name: eBay.com.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Electronic_Data_Systems" title="Electronic Data Systems">EDS</a> – <b>E</b>lectronic <b>D</b>ata <b>S</b>ystems, founded in 1962 by former IBM salesman <a href="/wiki/Ross_Perot" title="Ross Perot">Ross Perot</a>. According to the company history:<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> "He chose Electronic Data Systems from potential names he scribbled on a pledge envelope during a service at Highland Park Presbyterian Church in Dallas."</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/El_Al" title="El Al">El Al</a> - <a href="/wiki/Hebrew_language" title="Hebrew language">Hebrew</a>: אל על‎, "To the Skies" or "Skywards", <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: إل-عال</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Eidos_Interactive" class="mw-redirect" title="Eidos Interactive">Eidos</a> – named from a Greek word meaning "species".</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Eletropaulo" class="mw-redirect" title="Eletropaulo">Eletropaulo</a> – one of the largest Brazilian companies in electricity generation and distribution, its name derives from Companhia de Electricidade de São Paulo.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Elron_(rail_transit)" title="Elron (rail transit)">Elron</a> - from Estonian "<b>el</b>ektri<b>ron</b>g<i> ("electrical train").</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Embraer" title="Embraer">Embraer</a> – <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazilian</a> aircraft manufacturer, its name is an abbreviation of <b>Em</b>presa <b>Br</b>asileira de <b>Aer</b>onáutica (Brazilian Aeronautics Company).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Empresa_Brasileira_de_Pesquisa_Agropecu%C3%A1ria" class="mw-redirect" title="Empresa Brasileira de Pesquisa Agropecuária">EMBRAPA</a> – Brazilian state agricultural research and development company, its name is an abbreviation of <b>Em</b>presa <b>Bra</b>sileira de <b>P</b>esquisa <b>A</b>gropecuária (Brazilian Agriculture Research Company).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Telmex" title="Telmex">EMBRATEL</a> – abbreviation of <b>Em</b>presa <b>Bra</b>sileira de <b>Tel</b>ecomunicações (Brazilian Telecommunications Company). Brazil's largest telecommunications company, it was a <a href="/wiki/State_monopoly" title="State monopoly">state monopoly</a> until 1992 when it was privatized and sold to <a href="/wiki/MCI_Inc." title="MCI Inc.">MCI</a>, then later resold to <a href="/wiki/Telmex" title="Telmex">Telmex</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/EMC_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="EMC Corporation">EMC Corporation</a> – named from the initials of the founders, Richard <b>E</b>gan and Roger <b>M</b>arino. There has long been a rumor that another partner provided the third letter (C). Other reports indicate the C stands for <b>C</b>ompany. EMC adopted the EMC² notation to refer to Einstein's famous equation, <a href="/wiki/Mass-energy_equivalence" class="mw-redirect" title="Mass-energy equivalence"><i>E</i>&nbsp;=&nbsp;<i>mc</i>²</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/EMI" title="EMI">EMI</a> – formerly Electric and Musical Industries Ltd.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Emporis" title="Emporis">Emporis</a> – <b>Empor</b> comes from the German and means "aloft, rising"; one of the world's largest providers of data concerning buildings</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Seiko_Epson" title="Seiko Epson">Epson</a> – Epson Seiko Corporation, the Japanese printer and peripheral manufacturer, was named from "<b>Son</b> of <b>E</b>lectronic <b>P</b>rinter" after a highly successful model, the EP-101.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Equifax" title="Equifax">Equifax</a> – from <b>equi</b>table and <b>fact</b>ual</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ericsson" title="Ericsson">Ericsson</a> – <i>Telefonaktiebolaget LM Ericsson</i> is named after its founder <a href="/wiki/Lars_Magnus_Ericsson" title="Lars Magnus Ericsson">Lars Magnus Ericsson</a>, who opened a telegraph equipment repair shop in Stockholm, Sweden, in 1876<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ernst_%26_Young" title="Ernst &amp; Young">Ernst &amp; Young</a> – named for the company's founders, A.C. <b>Ernst</b> and Arthur <b>Young</b></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a> – <b>E</b>ntertainment and <b>S</b>ports <b>P</b>rogramming <b>N</b>etwork</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Environmental_Systems_Research_Institute" class="mw-redirect" title="Environmental Systems Research Institute">ESRI</a> – <b>E</b>nvironmental <b>S</b>ystems <b>R</b>esearch <b>I</b>nstitute, the first geographic information system (GIS) software company founded by Jack and Laura Dangermond in Redlands, California, in 1969</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Esso" title="Esso">Esso</a> – enunciation of the initials S.O. in <b>S</b>tandard <b>O</b>il of New Jersey</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Etsy" title="Etsy">Etsy</a> – founder Rob Kalin said that he named the site Etsy because he "wanted a nonsense word because I wanted to build the brand from scratch. I was watching Fellini's 8 ½ and writing down what I was hearing. In Italian, you say 'etsi' a lot. It means 'oh, yes' (actually it's "eh, si"). And in Latin and French, it means 'what if.'"<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Evernote" title="Evernote">Evernote</a> – combination of the words for<b>ever</b> and <b>note</b> to indicate the core service that the app provides</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/ExxonMobil" title="ExxonMobil">Exxon</a> – name contrived by Esso (Standard Oil of New Jersey) in the early 1970s to create a neutral but distinctive label for the company. Within days, Exxon was being called the "double cross company" but this eventually subsided. (Esso is a trademark of ExxonMobil.) Esso could not use its name in parts of the U.S. because of restrictions dating to the 1911 Standard Oil <a href="/wiki/Antitrust" class="mw-redirect" title="Antitrust">antitrust</a> decision.</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="F">F</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_company_name_etymologies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: F">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/F5_Networks" title="F5 Networks">F5 Networks</a> – originally <i>F5 Labs</i> – taken from the <a href="/wiki/Fujita_scale" title="Fujita scale">Fujita scale</a> of ratings for tornado intensity, where <i>F5</i> is the most intense to be used in normal practice even though the scale can physically describe up to <i>F12</i> which corresponds to wind velocities of Mach 1.0.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a> – name stems from the colloquial name of books given to newly enrolled students at the start of the academic year by university administrations in the US with the intention of helping students to get to know each other better.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fair_Isaac_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Fair Isaac Corporation">Fair Isaac Corporation</a> – named after founders Bill <b>Fair</b> and Earl <b>Isaac</b></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Foras_Aiseanna_Saothair" class="mw-redirect" title="Foras Aiseanna Saothair">FAS</a> – abbreviation for <a href="/wiki/Foras_%C3%81iseanna_Saothair" title="Foras Áiseanna Saothair">Foras Áiseanna Saothair</a> (<i>Labour Facilities Foundation</i>).  <b>Fás</b> means <i>grow</i> in Irish.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fazer" title="Fazer">Fazer</a> – Finnish food company named after its founder, <a href="/wiki/Karl_Fazer" title="Karl Fazer">Karl Fazer</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/French_Connection_(clothing)" title="French Connection (clothing)">FCUK</a> – <b>F</b>rench <b>C</b>onnection <b>U</b>nited <b>K</b>ingdom</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/FedEx" title="FedEx">FedEx</a> – abbreviation of <b>Fed</b>eral <b>Ex</b>press Corporation, the company's original name<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fegime" title="Fegime">Fegime</a> – abbreviation for "Fédération Européenne des Grossistes Indépendants" (European Federation of Independent Electrical Wholesalers)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ferodo" title="Ferodo">Ferodo</a> – anagram of the name of its founder, Herbert <b>Froode</b></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ferrari" title="Ferrari">Ferrari</a> – from the name of its founder, <a href="/wiki/Enzo_Ferrari" title="Enzo Ferrari">Enzo Ferrari</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fiat" class="mw-redirect" title="Fiat">Fiat</a> – acronym of <b>F</b>abbrica <b>I</b>taliana <b>A</b>utomobili <b>T</b>orino (Italian Automobile Factory of Turin)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Finnair" title="Finnair">Finnair</a> – from "Finland" and "air". Originally called "Aero <a href="/wiki/Osakeyhti%C3%B6" title="Osakeyhtiö">Osakeyhtiö</a>", which led to its international flight code, "AY".</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Firestone_Tire_and_Rubber_Company" title="Firestone Tire and Rubber Company">Firestone</a> – named after its founder, <a href="/wiki/Harvey_Firestone" class="mw-redirect" title="Harvey Firestone">Harvey Firestone</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fisher-Price" title="Fisher-Price">Fisher-Price</a> – toy company named after two of its three founders: <a href="/wiki/Herman_Fisher" title="Herman Fisher">Herman Fisher</a>, <a href="/wiki/Irving_Price" title="Irving Price">Irving Price</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Helen_Schelle" title="Helen Schelle">Helen Schelle</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> It became a Mattel subsidiary in 1993.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fiskars" title="Fiskars">Fiskars</a> – from the town of <a href="/wiki/Fiskars,_Finland" title="Fiskars, Finland">Fiskars</a>, where the company was founded.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Five_Guys" title="Five Guys">Five Guys</a> – American restaurant chain founded by "five guys" – Jerry Murrell and his four sons. The "five guys" would later become the Murrell sons, after Jerry and his wife Janie had a fifth son two years after opening their first restaurant.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Restaurant_Business_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Restaurant_Business-59">[59]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fluke_Corporation" title="Fluke Corporation">Fluke</a> – named after its founder, John Fluke, Sr.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fonterra" title="Fonterra">Fonterra</a> – glosses its own name as "spring from the land".<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> That would match a faux-Latin combination of <i>fons</i> (stem <i>font-</i>) conveying the idea of a fountain or spring, and <i>terra</i>, meaning earth, land, or ground.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ford_Motor_Company" title="Ford Motor Company">Ford Motor Company</a> – named after its founder, <a href="/wiki/Henry_Ford" title="Henry Ford">Henry Ford</a>, who introduced automobile mass production in 1914.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Forrester_Research" title="Forrester Research">Forrester Research</a> – from the family name of the mother of the founder George Forrester Colony.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/FranklinCovey" title="FranklinCovey">FranklinCovey</a> – named after <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Franklin" title="Benjamin Franklin">Benjamin Franklin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Covey" title="Stephen Covey">Stephen Covey</a>. The company was formed from the 1997 merger of FranklinQuest and the Covey Leadership Center.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fuji_Heavy_Industries" class="mw-redirect" title="Fuji Heavy Industries">Fuji</a> – named after Mount Fuji, the highest mountain in Japan</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fujitsu" title="Fujitsu">Fujitsu</a> – originally the data division of <a href="/wiki/Fuji_Electric" title="Fuji Electric">Fuji Electric</a>, which was a joint venture between <a href="/wiki/Furukawa_Electric" title="Furukawa Electric">Furukawa Electric</a> and <a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">Siemens</a>. The <b>tsu</b> comes from tsūshinki, meaning data equipment.</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="G">G</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_company_name_etymologies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: G">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Gallup_(company)" title="Gallup (company)">Gallup</a> – polling company named after its founder, <a href="/wiki/George_Gallup" title="George Gallup">George Gallup</a>. After his death in 1984, the company was sold to Selection Research, Incorporated (SRI).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Garmin" title="Garmin">Garmin</a> – named after its founders, <b>Gar</b>y Burrell and Dr. <b>Min</b> Kao</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gartner" title="Gartner">Gartner</a> – named after its founder, Gideon Gartner, who left the firm in 1992 to start Giga (named from <b>Gi</b>deon <b>Ga</b>rtner)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gatti%27s_Pizza" title="Gatti's Pizza">Gatti's Pizza</a> – Gatti was the maiden name of Pat Eure, wife of company founder Jim Eure.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/GCap_Media" title="GCap Media">GCap Media</a> – named after the merger of the <a href="/wiki/GWR_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="GWR Group"><b>G</b>WR Group</a> and <a href="/wiki/Capital_Radio_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Capital Radio Group"><b>Cap</b>ital Radio Group</a> in May 2005. GWR was launched in 1985 after the merger of Radio West and <b>W</b>iltshire <b>R</b>adio.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/GEICO" title="GEICO">GEICO</a> – from <b>G</b>overnment <b>E</b>mployees <b>I</b>nsurance <b>Co</b>mpany</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Genentech" title="Genentech">Genentech</a> – from <b>Gen</b>etic <b>En</b>gineering <b>Tech</b>nology</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gerdau" title="Gerdau">Gerdau</a> – largest producer of long steel in the Americas, named from the surname of the founder, Johannes Heinrich Kaspar Gerdau</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gilead_Sciences" title="Gilead Sciences">Gilead Sciences</a> – pharmaceutical company named after <a href="/wiki/Gilead" title="Gilead">Gilead</a>, a biblical place name</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/GlaxoSmithKline" title="GlaxoSmithKline">Glaxo</a> – dried-milk company set up in <a href="/wiki/Bunnythorpe" title="Bunnythorpe">Bunnythorpe</a>, New Zealand, by <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Nathan" title="Joseph Nathan">Joseph Edward Nathan</a>. The company wanted to use the name "Lacto" but it was similar to some already in use. The company says: "By adding and changing letters, the name Glaxo evolved and was registered in October 1906."<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/GlaxoSmithKline" title="GlaxoSmithKline">GlaxoSmithKline</a> was a 2000 merger of <a href="/wiki/Glaxo_Wellcome" class="mw-redirect" title="Glaxo Wellcome">Glaxo Wellcome</a> and <a href="/wiki/Beecham_(pharmaceutical_company)" class="mw-redirect" title="Beecham (pharmaceutical company)">SmithKline Beecham</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Glock_Ges.m.b.H." title="Glock Ges.m.b.H.">Glock Ges.m.b.H.</a> – named after its founder, <a href="/wiki/Gaston_Glock" title="Gaston Glock">Gaston Glock</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Goodyear_Tire_and_Rubber_Company" title="Goodyear Tire and Rubber Company">Goodyear</a> – named after the founder of vulcanization, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Goodyear" title="Charles Goodyear">Charles Goodyear</a>, the Goodyear Tire and Rubber company was founded by Frank Seiberling in 1898</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a> – originally an accidental misspelling of the word "<a href="/wiki/Googol" title="Googol">googol</a>", settled upon because google.com was unregistered. Googol was proposed to reflect the company's mission to organize the immense amount of information available online.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Grey_Global_Group" title="Grey Global Group">Grey Global Group</a> – advertising and marketing agency supposed to have derived its name from the colour of the walls of its first office</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Groupon" title="Groupon">Groupon</a> – chief executive Andrew Mason used the derivation as his five-word acceptance speech at the 2011 Webby Awards ceremony: "It's short for group coupon."<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Grundig" title="Grundig">Grundig</a> – named after its founder, radio dealer-turned-manufacturer <a href="/wiki/Max_Grundig" title="Max Grundig">Max Grundig</a>, in 1945</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gucci" title="Gucci">Gucci</a> – named after its founder, <a href="/wiki/Guccio_Gucci" title="Guccio Gucci">Guccio Gucci</a>, who became familiar with high class luggage while working as a lift boy at the Savoy Hotel in London. He returned to Florence and started making travel bags and accessories, founding the House of Gucci in 1921.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gulfstream_Aerospace" title="Gulfstream Aerospace">Gulfstream Aerospace</a> – named after the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Stream" title="Gulf Stream">Gulf Stream</a> current that starts in the Gulf of Mexico and crosses the Atlantic.
