The company traces its origins to the <a href="/wiki/Grumman_Aircraft_Engineering_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Grumman Aircraft Engineering Corporation">Grumman Aircraft Engineering Corporation</a>, which was sold and renamed in 1985.</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="H">H</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_company_name_etymologies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: H">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/H%26M" title="H&amp;M">H&amp;M</a> – named from <b>H</b>ennes <b>&amp;</b> <b>M</b>auritz. In 1947, Swedish businessman Erling Persson established <i>Hennes</i>, a ladies' clothing store, in Västerås, Sweden. "Hennes" is Swedish for "hers". In 1968, Persson bought the Stockholm premises and inventory of a hunting equipment store called <i>Mauritz Widforss</i>. The inventory included a collection of men's clothing, which prompted Persson to expand into menswear.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/H%26R_Block" title="H&amp;R Block">H&amp;R Block</a> – after the founders, brothers <b>H</b>enry W. and <b>R</b>ichard <b>Bloch</b> (with "Bloch" changed to "Block" to avoid mispronunciation)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/H%C3%A4agen-Dazs" title="Häagen-Dazs">Häagen-Dazs</a> – name was invented in 1961 by ice-cream makers <a href="/wiki/Reuben_and_Rose_Mattus" title="Reuben and Rose Mattus">Reuben and Rose Mattus</a> of the Bronx "to convey an aura of the old-world traditions and craftsmanship"<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> The name has no meaning.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Haier" title="Haier">Haier</a> – Chinese 海 "sea" and 尔 (a <a href="/wiki/Transliteration" title="Transliteration">transliteration</a> character; also means "you" in <a href="/wiki/Literary_Chinese" class="mw-redirect" title="Literary Chinese">Literary Chinese</a>). Portion of transliteration of German Liebherr 利勃海尔.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Happy_Madison_Productions" title="Happy Madison Productions">Happy Madison Productions</a> – film and TV production company founded by Adam Sandler, its name is taken from the films <i><a href="/wiki/Happy_Gilmore" title="Happy Gilmore">Happy Gilmore</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Billy_Madison" title="Billy Madison">Billy Madison</a></i>, two of his box office successes.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Haribo" title="Haribo">Haribo</a> – from the name of the founder and the German home town of the company: <b>Ha</b>ns <b>Ri</b>egel, <a href="/wiki/Bonn" title="Bonn"><b>Bo</b>nn</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Harman_Kardon" title="Harman Kardon">Harman Kardon</a> – named after its founders Dr. Sidney Harman and Bernard Kardon</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Harpo_Productions" title="Harpo Productions">Harpo Productions</a> – production company founded by Oprah Winfrey; "Oprah" spelled backwards.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Harvey_Norman" title="Harvey Norman">Harvey Norman</a> – named after its founders <a href="/wiki/Gerry_Harvey" title="Gerry Harvey">Gerry Harvey</a> and Ian Norman</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hasbro" title="Hasbro">Hasbro</a> – founded by Henry and Helal Hassenfeld, the <b>Has</b>senfeld <b>Bro</b>thers</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/HBOS" title="HBOS">HBOS</a> – UK-based banking company formed by the merger of the <b>H</b>alifax and the <b>B</b>ank <b>o</b>f <b>S</b>cotland</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Housing_Development_Finance_Corporation" title="Housing Development Finance Corporation">HDFC</a> – Housing Development Finance Corporation, Indian mortgage company.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hesburger" title="Hesburger">Hesburger</a> – from <b>Hes</b>e, the nickname of the company's founder Heikki Salmela, and ham<b>burger</b></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hess_Corporation" title="Hess Corporation">Hess Corporation</a> – named after its founder <a href="/wiki/Leon_Hess" title="Leon Hess">Leon Hess</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hispano-Suiza" title="Hispano-Suiza">Hispano-Suiza</a> – former Spanish luxury automotive and engineering firm; its name – literally meaning "Spanish-Swiss" – refers to Spanish origin of the company and Swiss origin of its head engineer <a href="/wiki/Marc_Birkigt" title="Marc Birkigt">Marc Birkigt</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hitachi,_Ltd." class="mw-redirect" title="Hitachi, Ltd.">Hitachi</a> – old place name, literally "sunrise"</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/HMV" title="HMV">HMV</a> – from "His Master's Voice", which appeared in 1899 as the title of a painting of Nipper, a Jack Russell terrier, listening to a gramophone</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hoechst_AG" title="Hoechst AG">Hoechst</a> – from the name of a district in <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Honda" title="Honda">Honda</a> – from the name of its founder, <a href="/wiki/Soichiro_Honda" title="Soichiro Honda">Soichiro Honda</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Honeywell" title="Honeywell">Honeywell</a> – from the name of <a href="/wiki/Mark_Honeywell" class="mw-redirect" title="Mark Honeywell">Mark Honeywell</a>, founder of Honeywell Heating Specialty Co. It later merged with Minneapolis Heat Regulator Company and was finally called Honeywell Inc. in 1963.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hospira" title="Hospira">Hospira</a> – name, selected by the company's employees, is derived from the words hospital, spirit, inspire and the Latin word spero, which means hope. It expresses the hope and optimism that are critical in the healthcare industry.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hotmail" class="mw-redirect" title="Hotmail">Hotmail</a> – founder <a href="/wiki/Jack_Smith_(Hotmail)" title="Jack Smith (Hotmail)">Jack Smith</a> got the idea of accessing e-mail via the web from a computer anywhere in the world. When <a href="/wiki/Sabeer_Bhatia" title="Sabeer Bhatia">Sabeer Bhatia</a> came up with the business plan for the mail service he tried all kinds of names ending in 'mail' and finally settled for Hotmail as it included the letters "<a href="/wiki/HTML" title="HTML">HTML</a>" – the markup language used to write web pages. It was initially referred to as HoTMaiL with selective upper casing. (At one time, if you clicked on Hotmail's 'mail' tab, you would have seen "HoTMaiL" in the URL.) Hotmail addresses now use Microsoft's Outlook.com service.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hewlett-Packard_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Hewlett-Packard Company">HP</a> – co-founders <a href="/wiki/Bill_Hewlett" title="Bill Hewlett">Bill <b>H</b>ewlett</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dave_Packard" class="mw-redirect" title="Dave Packard">Dave <b>P</b>ackard</a> tossed a coin to decide whether their company would be called Hewlett-Packard or Packard-Hewlett. In November 2015, Hewlett-Packard split into two listed companies: HP Inc and Hewlett Packard Enterprise Co.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/HSBC" title="HSBC">HSBC</a> – <b>H</b>ongkong and <b>S</b>hanghai <b>B</b>anking <b>C</b>orporation.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/HTC" title="HTC">HTC</a> – contraction of its original corporate name, <b>H</b>igh <b>T</b>ech <b>C</b>omputer Corporation.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Huawei" title="Huawei">Huawei</a> – Chinese <a href="/wiki/%E5%8D%8E" class="mw-redirect" title="华">华</a> (hua) and 为 (wei) as a whole may be translated as "splendid act" or "China is able"; Hua can mean "splendid" (literally "flowery beauty") or "China", while wei can mean "action" or "achievement".</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hudson%27s_Bay_Company" title="Hudson's Bay Company">Hudson's Bay Company</a> – in 1670, a Royal Charter granted the lands of the Hudson Bay watershed to "the Governor and Company of Adventurers of England trading into Hudson Bay." The company ceded the territory to Canada in 1870.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hyundai_Group" title="Hyundai Group">Hyundai</a> – connotes the sense of "the present age" or "modernity" in Korean</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="I">I</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_company_name_etymologies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: I">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a> – named by Tom (Thomas John) Watson Sr, an ex-employee of National Cash Register (<a href="/wiki/NCR_Corporation" title="NCR Corporation">NCR Corporation</a>). To one-up them in all respects, he called his company <b>I</b>nternational <b>B</b>usiness <b>M</b>achines.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/International_Computers_Limited" title="International Computers Limited">ICL</a> – abbreviation for <a href="/wiki/International_Computers_Limited" title="International Computers Limited">International Computers Limited</a>, once the UK's largest computer company but now a service arm of Fujitsu, of Japan.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/IG_Farben" title="IG Farben">IG Farben</a> – <b>I</b>nteressen-<b>G</b>emeinschaft <b>Farben</b>industrie AG was so named because the constituent German companies produced <a href="/wiki/Dye" title="Dye">dyestuffs</a> among many other chemical compounds. The consortium is most known today for its central participation in the World War II <a href="/wiki/Holocaust" class="mw-redirect" title="Holocaust">Holocaust</a>, as it made the <a href="/wiki/Zyklon_B" title="Zyklon B">Zyklon B</a> gas used in the <a href="/wiki/Gas_chambers" class="mw-redirect" title="Gas chambers">gas chambers</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/IGN_Entertainment" class="mw-redirect" title="IGN Entertainment">IGN Entertainment</a> – IGN Entertainment is an online entertainment media outlet. Its name comes from its origin as a spin-off of <a href="/wiki/Imagine_Media" class="mw-redirect" title="Imagine Media">Imagine Media</a> and used to stand for <b>I</b>magine <b>G</b>ames <b>N</b>etwork.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Iiyama_(company)" title="Iiyama (company)">Iiyama</a> – manufacturer of monitors and TVs, named after the Japanese city, Iiyama</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/IKEA" title="IKEA">IKEA</a> – composite of the first letters in the Swedish founder <a href="/wiki/Ingvar_Kamprad" title="Ingvar Kamprad">Ingvar Kamprad</a>'s name in addition to the first letters of the names of the property and the village in which he grew up: <b>I</b>ngvar <b>K</b>amprad <b>E</b>lmtaryd <b>A</b>gunnaryd.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/IMI_plc" title="IMI plc">IMI</a> – Imperial Metal Industries, split off from Imperial Chemical Industries</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/InBev" title="InBev">InBev</a> – name was created after the merger of the Belgian company <a href="/wiki/Interbrew" title="Interbrew"><b>In</b>terbrew</a> with Brazilian <a href="/wiki/Ambev" title="Ambev">Am<b>bev</b></a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Inditex" title="Inditex">Inditex</a> – Spanish group named from <b>In</b>dustria de <b>Di</b>seño <b>Tex</b>til (Textile Design Industry).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Infineon_Technologies" title="Infineon Technologies">Infineon Technologies</a> – derived from <b>Inf</b>inity and A<b>eon</b>. The name was given to <a href="/wiki/Siemens_AG" class="mw-redirect" title="Siemens AG">Siemens's</a> Semiconductor branch (called Siemens HL or Siemens SC/SSC) when it was spun off.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ingenico" title="Ingenico">Ingenico</a> – electronic payment device manufacturer based in Paris and named from the French <b>Ingeni</b>eux <b>Co</b>mpagnie (Ingenious Company)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Inktomi_(company)" class="mw-redirect" title="Inktomi (company)">Inktomi</a> – internet search engine, acquired by Yahoo! in 2002; named after <a href="/wiki/Iktomi" title="Iktomi">Iktomi</a>, a spider-trickster spirit from Lakota Indian legends</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Intel_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Intel Corporation">Intel</a> – Robert Noyce and Gordon Moore initially incorporated their company as N M Electronics. Someone suggested Moore Noyce Electronics but it sounded too close to "more noise". Later, Integrated Electronics was proposed but it had already been taken, so they used the initial syllables (<b>INT</b>egrated <a href="/wiki/Electronics" title="Electronics"><b>EL</b>ectronics</a>). To avoid potential conflicts with other companies with similar names, Intel purchased the name rights for $15,000 from a company called Intelco. (Source: Intel 15 Years Corporate Anniversary Brochure)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/ITC_(company)" class="mw-redirect" title="ITC (company)">ITC</a> – established in 1910 as the <b>Imperial Tobacco Company</b>.</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="J">J</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_company_name_etymologies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: J">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/J._C._Penney" title="J. C. Penney">J. C. Penney</a> – from <a href="/wiki/James_Cash_Penney" title="James Cash Penney"><b>J</b>ames <b>C</b>ash Penney</a>, founder of the department store chain.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/J2TV" class="mw-redirect" title="J2TV">J2TV</a> – television and film production company formed by <i><a href="/wiki/Malcolm_in_the_Middle" title="Malcolm in the Middle">Malcolm in the Middle</a></i> actor <b>J</b>ustin Berfield and producer <b>J</b>ason Felts</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Japan_Airlines" title="Japan Airlines">JAL</a> – from <b>J</b>apan <b>A</b>ir<b>l</b>ines</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jat_Airways" title="Jat Airways">Jat Airways</a> – founded in 1927 as "Aeroput" (Airway in Serbian). From 1947, it was known as JAT (<b>J</b>ugoslovenski <b>A</b>ero <b>T</b>ransport). After the break-up of the former Yugoslavia (and after Federal Republic of Yugoslavia changed its name to Serbia and Montenegro), the company kept the name, Jat, but not as an abbreviation.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jawa_Motors" class="mw-redirect" title="Jawa Motors">Jawa Motors</a> – from <b>Ja</b>neček (the owner) and <b>Wa</b>nderer (the motorcycle product)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/JBL_(company)" class="mw-redirect" title="JBL (company)">JBL</a> – from <b>J</b>ames <b>B</b> <b>L</b>ansing, an electronics designer</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Johnson_%26_Johnson" title="Johnson &amp; Johnson">Johnson &amp; Johnson</a> – originally a partnership between brothers James Wood Johnson and Edward Mead Johnson in 1885, the addition of brother Robert Wood Johnson I led to formal incorporation as Johnson &amp; Johnson in 1887.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jordache" title="Jordache">Jordache</a> – from the first names of the Nakash brothers who founded the company: <b>Jo</b>e, <b>R</b>alph, <b>D</b>avid (Ralph's first son), <b>A</b>vi, plus <b>che</b>, after the second syllable of "Nakash"<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/JVC" title="JVC">JVC</a> – <b>J</b>apan <b>V</b>ictor <b>C</b>ompany (Victor Company of Japan, Ltd) was founded in 1927 as a US subsidiary, The Victor Talking Machine Company of Japan, Limited. JVC developed the VHS video cassette format.</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="K">K</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_company_name_etymologies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: K">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Kalev_(company)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kalev (company)">Kalev</a> – after <a href="/wiki/Kalev_(mythology)" title="Kalev (mythology)"><b>Kalev</b></a>, the character from <a href="/wiki/Estonian_mythology" title="Estonian mythology">Estonian mythology</a> and father of the protagonist in the <a href="/wiki/National_epic" title="National epic">national epic</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Kalevipoeg" title="Kalevipoeg">Kalevipoeg</a></i> ("Son of Kalev").</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kamaz" title="Kamaz">Kamaz</a> – after <a href="/wiki/Kama_River" title="Kama River">Kama River</a>; long form <i><b>Kam</b>skiy <b>a</b>vtomobilny <b>z</b>avod</i> (Kama Automobile Plant)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kawasaki_Heavy_Industries" title="Kawasaki Heavy Industries">Kawasaki</a> – from the name of its founder, <a href="/wiki/Shozo_Kawasaki" class="mw-redirect" title="Shozo Kawasaki">Shozo Kawasaki</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/KFC" title="KFC">KFC</a> – short for <b>K</b>entucky <b>F</b>ried <b>C</b>hicken</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kenvelo" title="Kenvelo">Kenvelo</a> – clothing retailer founded in the Czech Republic by Israel-born owner Dany Himi. Various names were proposed to managers, but some said "yes" and some "no". David Dahan came up with yesandno or <b>Ken</b> (yes), <b>ve</b> (and) <b>lo</b> (no) in Hebrew (כן ולא).<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kenwood_Electronics" class="mw-redirect" title="Kenwood Electronics">Kenwood Electronics</a> – Bill Kasuga was a partner in a firm that imported Japanese-made audio products from Trio Corporation to the United States. Kasuga wanted to create a trustworthy and Western-sounding name for products sold by his importing company as he was confident of the quality of Trio's products in a period when Japanese-made goods were considered inferior. He came up with Kenwood by combining "Ken" – a name common to Japan and North America that had proven acceptable to American consumers in the name of <a href="/wiki/Kenmore_Appliances" class="mw-redirect" title="Kenmore Appliances">Kenmore Appliances</a> – and "wood", referring to the durable substance as well as suggesting a relation to <a href="/wiki/Hollywood" title="Hollywood">Hollywood</a>. Trio Corporation renamed itself Kenwood in 1986.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kenwood_Limited" title="Kenwood Limited">Kenwood Limited</a> – named after Kenneth (Ken) Wood, who founded this kitchenware company in the UK in 1947 with wartime colleague Roger Laurence as Woodlau Industries<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> It is not related to <a href="/wiki/Kenwood_Electronics" class="mw-redirect" title="Kenwood Electronics">Kenwood Electronics</a>, which started as Kasuga Radio Co in Japan in 1946 and became Trio Corporation in 1960.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kenworth" title="Kenworth">Kenworth</a> Truck Company – named after the two principal stockholders Harry <b>Ken</b>t and Edgar <b>Worth</b>ington</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Keurig" title="Keurig">Keurig</a> – from the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a> word <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/keurig" class="extiw" title="wikt:keurig">keurig</a>. Company co-founder John Sylvan said that once his coffee pod system worked, "he looked up the word excellence in Dutch — because 'everyone likes the Dutch'." <sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kia_Motors" title="Kia Motors">Kia Motors</a> – "Kia" (起亞) roughly translates as "Rising from Asia" in <a href="/wiki/Hanja" title="Hanja">Hanja</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kinko%27s" class="mw-redirect" title="Kinko's">Kinko's</a> – from the college nickname of founder, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Orfalea" title="Paul Orfalea">Paul Orfalea</a>. He was called Kinko because he had curly red hair. The company was bought by FedEx for $2.4&nbsp;billion in 2004.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kmart" title="Kmart">Kmart</a> – named for <a href="/wiki/Sebastian_S._Kresge" class="mw-redirect" title="Sebastian S. Kresge">Sebastian S. Kresge</a>, who opened the first Kmart in 1962 as a division of his S. S. Kresge Company. The company became Kmart Corporation in 1977. After purchasing <a href="/wiki/Sears" title="Sears">Sears, Roebuck &amp; Company</a> in 2005, the merged company became <a href="/wiki/Sears_Holdings_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Sears Holdings Corporation">Sears Holdings Corporation</a>, with Kmart continuing as a discount store chain within the new structure.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Eastman_Kodak" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastman Kodak">Kodak</a> – both the Kodak camera and the name were the invention of founder <a href="/wiki/George_Eastman" title="George Eastman">George Eastman</a>. The letter "K" was a favorite with Eastman; he felt it a strong and incisive letter. He tried out various combinations of words starting and ending with "K". He saw three advantages in the name. It had the merits of a trademark word, would not be mis-pronounced and the name did not resemble anything in the art. There is a misconception that the name was chosen because of its similarity to the sound produced by the shutter of the camera.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Komatsu_Limited" title="Komatsu Limited">Komatsu</a> – Japanese construction vehicle manufacturer named from the city of Komatsu, Ishikawa, where it was founded in 1917</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kone" title="Kone">Kone</a> – Means "machine" or "device" in <a href="/wiki/Finnish_language" title="Finnish language">Finnish</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Konica" title="Konica">Konica</a> – earlier known as <b>Koni</b>shiroku <b>Ko</b>gaku. Konishiroku in turn is the short for <b>Konishi</b>ya <b>Roku</b>beiten, which was the first name of the company established by Rokusaburo Sugiura in the 1850s.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Korg" title="Korg">Korg</a> – named from the surnames of the founders, Tsutomu <b>K</b>atoh and Tadashi <b>O</b>sanai, combined with the letters "rg" from the word "organ"</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/KPMG" title="KPMG">KPMG</a> – from the last names of the founders of the firms which combined to form the cooperative: <a href="/wiki/Piet_Klijnveld" title="Piet Klijnveld">Piet <b>K</b>lijnveld</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_Barclay_Peat" title="William Barclay Peat">William Barclay <b>P</b>eat</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Marwick" title="James Marwick">James <b>M</b>arwick</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Reinhard_Goerdeler" title="Reinhard Goerdeler">Reinhard <b>G</b>oerdeler</a><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kroger" title="Kroger">Kroger</a> – American supermarket chain named after its founder, Barney Kroger</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/KUKA" title="KUKA">KUKA</a> – founded in 1898 in Augsburg, Germany as <b>K</b>eller <b>U</b>nd <b>K</b>nappich <b>A</b>ugsburg, it shortened its name to KUKA. Today, it is a manufacturer of industrial robots and automation systems.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kyocera" title="Kyocera">Kyocera</a> – from <b>Kyo</b>to <b>Cera</b>mics, after Kyoto in Japan</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="L">L</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_company_name_etymologies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: L">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/LaCie" title="LaCie">LaCie</a> – from the <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> phrase <i>la cie</i>, meaning "the company"</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lada" title="Lada">Lada</a> – from the name of a Slavic goddess, and used as a trading name by Russian automobile manufacturer <a href="/wiki/AvtoVAZ" title="AvtoVAZ">AvtoVAZ</a> (АВТОВАЗ in Russian). VAZ is derived from <b>V</b>olzhsky <b>A</b>utomobilny <b>Z</b>avod.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lanc%C3%B4me" title="Lancôme">Lancôme</a> – began in 1935, when its founder, Armand Petitjean, was exploring the ruins of a castle, Le Chateau de Lancôme (<a href="/wiki/Loir-et-Cher" title="Loir-et-Cher">Loir-et-Cher</a>) while vacationing in the French countryside. Petitjean's inspiration for the company's symbol, a rose, was the many wild roses growing around the castle.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/LCL_S.A." title="LCL S.A.">LCL</a> – from <i>Le Crédit Lyonnais</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lego" title="Lego">Lego</a> – combination of the Danish "leg godt", which means to "play well".<sup id="cite_ref-lego_home_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lego_home-72">[72]</a></sup>  Lego also means "I put together" in Latin, but <a href="/wiki/Lego_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Lego Group">Lego Group</a> claims this is only a coincidence and the etymology of the word is entirely Danish. Years before the little plastic brick was invented, Lego manufactured wooden toys.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lenovo_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Lenovo Group">Lenovo Group</a> – <a href="/wiki/Portmanteau" title="Portmanteau">portmanteau</a> of "Le-" (from former name Legend) and "novo", pseudo-Latin for "new". This Chinese company took over IBM's PC division.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lesney_Products" title="Lesney Products">Lesney Products</a> – named from the founders <b>Les</b>lie Smith and Rod<b>ney</b> Smith, who were school friends but not related. This British company made the Matchbox series of die-cast toys, similar to Dinky toys.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Level_3_Communications" title="Level 3 Communications">Level 3 Communications</a> – "Level 3" is a reference to the <a href="/wiki/Network_layer" title="Network layer">network layer</a> of the <a href="/wiki/OSI_model" title="OSI model">OSI model</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lexmark" title="Lexmark">Lexmark</a> – in the 1980s, IBM wanted to spin off its printer and typewriter businesses. The main production facility for this business segment was in <a href="/wiki/Lexington,_Kentucky" title="Lexington, Kentucky">Lexington, Kentucky</a>, and the code name for the spinoff was <b>Lex</b>ington <b>Mark</b>eting.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/LG_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="LG Group">LG</a> – from the combination of two popular Korean brands, <b>L</b>ucky and <b>G</b>oldstar. (In Mexico, publicists explained the name change as an abbreviation to <b>Linea Goldstar</b>, Spanish for <b>Goldstar Line</b>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lidl" title="Lidl">Lidl</a> – Named after painter and retired schoolteacher Ludwig Lidl, from whom <a href="/wiki/Dieter_Schwarz" title="Dieter Schwarz">Dieter Schwarz</a>, the son of company founder Josef Schwarz bought the rights to the name for 1,000 <a href="/wiki/German_mark" class="mw-redirect" title="German mark">German marks</a>. Schwarz originally wanted to use the name of his father's former business partner A. Lidl, but legal reasons prevented it. Schwarz did not want to name the company after himself as <i>Schwarzmarkt</i> means "<a href="/wiki/Black_market" title="Black market">black market</a>" in <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lionbridge" title="Lionbridge">Lionbridge</a> – word "localisation", which is the service this company offers, is often shortened to L10N. That is the first letter of the word and the last letter of the word, with 10 letters missing in between, hence L 10 N, which looks like lion. Bridge is the second part of the word as translation 'bridges' gap between people and markets that do not have a common language.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lionhead_Studios" title="Lionhead Studios">Lionhead Studios</a> – games studio named after Mark Webley's pet hamster, which died a week before the company was founded<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> Webley worked for <a href="/wiki/Bullfrog_Productions" title="Bullfrog Productions">Bullfrog</a>, and co-founded Lionhead with <a href="/wiki/Peter_Molyneux" title="Peter Molyneux">Peter Molyneux</a>, Tim Rance and Steve Jackson in July 1997. Microsoft bought the company in April 2006.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Loblaws" title="Loblaws">Loblaws</a> – Canadian supermarket chain named for founder <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Loblaw" title="Theodore Loblaw">Theodore Loblaw</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Martin" title="Lockheed Martin">Lockheed Martin</a> – aerospace manufacturer, a combination of <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Corporation" title="Lockheed Corporation">Lockheed Corporation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Martin_Marietta" title="Martin Marietta">Martin Marietta</a>, which was a combination of <a href="/wiki/Glenn_L._Martin_Company" title="Glenn L. Martin Company">Glenn L. Martin Company</a> and <a href="/wiki/American-Marietta_Corporation" title="American-Marietta Corporation">American-Marietta Corporation</a>, named for <a href="/wiki/Marietta,_Ohio" title="Marietta, Ohio">Marietta, Ohio</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/LoJack" title="LoJack">LoJack</a> – "LoJack" (the stolen-vehicle recovery system) is a pun on the word "hijack" (to steal a vehicle).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Longines" title="Longines">Longines</a> – in 1862 the new company "Ancienne Maison Auguste Agassiz, Ernest Francillon, Successeur" was born. At that time watchmaking in the area used the skills of people working outside the "comptoir d'établissage", often at home. In 1866 Ernest Francillon bought two plots of land on the right bank of the river Suze at the place called "Les Longines" and brought all of the watchmaking skills under one roof. This was the first "Longines factory".</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lonsdale_(clothing)" title="Lonsdale (clothing)">Lonsdale</a> – boxing equipment manufacturer named after the <a href="/wiki/Lonsdale_Belt" title="Lonsdale Belt">Lonsdale Belt</a>, a boxing trophy donated by the English Lord Lonsdale.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/L%27Or%C3%A9al" title="L'Oréal">L'Oréal</a> – in 1907, Eugène Schueller, a young French chemist, developed an innovative hair-color formula. He called his improved hair dye Auréole.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/LOT_Polish_Airlines" title="LOT Polish Airlines">LOT</a> – LOT Polish Airlines. "Lot" in Polish means "flight".</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lotus_Software" title="Lotus Software">Lotus Software</a> – <a href="/wiki/Mitch_Kapor" title="Mitch Kapor">Mitch Kapor</a> named his company after the <a href="/wiki/Lotus_Position" class="mw-redirect" title="Lotus Position">Lotus Position</a> or 'Padmasana'. Kapor used to be a teacher of <a href="/wiki/Transcendental_Meditation_technique" title="Transcendental Meditation technique">Transcendental Meditation technique</a> as taught by Maharishi Mahesh Yogi.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/LTX" title="LTX">LTX</a> – semiconductor test equipment company formed by people who left Teradyne, and said to stand for "Leave Teradyne by Xmas" or possibly "Left Teradyne at Xmas" (Christmas). LTX merged with Credence Systems Corporation and is now part of Xcerra Corporation.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lucent_Technologies" class="mw-redirect" title="Lucent Technologies">Lucent Technologies</a> – spin-off from AT&amp;T, it was named Lucent (meaning "luminous" or "glowing with light") because "light as a metaphor for visionary thinking reflected the company's operating and guiding business philosophy", according to the Landor Associates staff who chose the name.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> It was taken over by Alcatel to form Alcatel-Lucent in 2006.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ludicorp" title="Ludicorp">Ludicorp</a> – named from the Latin <i>lūdere</i> (to play)<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> because the intention was to develop an online game, though co-founders <a href="/wiki/Stewart_Butterfield" title="Stewart Butterfield">Stewart Butterfield</a> and <a href="/wiki/Caterina_Fake" title="Caterina Fake">Caterina Fake</a> developed a successful photo-sharing website. They wanted to call it Flicker, but Fake dropped the "e" when the owner of Flicker.com wouldn't sell them the domain name.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> Ludicorp sold Flickr to <a href="/wiki/Yahoo" class="mw-redirect" title="Yahoo">Yahoo</a> in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> The Oath division of <a href="/wiki/Verizon" class="mw-redirect" title="Verizon">Verizon</a> sold Flickr to SmugMug in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lufthansa" title="Lufthansa">Lufthansa</a> – founded as <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Luft_Hansa" title="Deutsche Luft Hansa">Deutsche Luft Hansa</a> in 1926,<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> where "Deutsche Luft" means "German Air" and Hansa refers to the <a href="/wiki/Hanseatic_League" title="Hanseatic League">Hanseatic League</a> of medieval guilds. It was renamed Lufthansa in 1933.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lukoil" title="Lukoil">Lukoil</a> – from the first letters of the three companies that merged to form the <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russian</a> <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">oil</a> giant: <b>L</b>angepasneftegaz, <b>U</b>raineftegaz, and <b>K</b>ogalymneftegaz, plus the English word "oil"</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/LVMH" title="LVMH">LVMH</a> – from the initials of the 1987 merger of <b>L</b>ouis <b>V</b>uitton and <b>M</b>oët <b>H</b>ennessy. The former was named after <a href="/wiki/Louis_Vuitton" title="Louis Vuitton">Louis Vuitton</a> while the latter was created in the 1971 merger of two earlier companies, Moët &amp; Chandon (champagne) and Hennessy (cognac).<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lycos" title="Lycos">Lycos</a> – web search engine company founded in 1994 and named from <i>Lycosidae</i>, the family of <a href="/wiki/Wolf_spider" title="Wolf spider">wolf spiders</a><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="M">M</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_company_name_etymologies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: M">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Maggi" title="Maggi">Maggi</a> – food company named after its founder, Julius Maggi. It was taken over by Nestlé in 1947 and survives as a brand name.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mailchimp" title="Mailchimp">Mailchimp</a> – the email marketing company was originally going to be called Chimpmail but the domain was taken, so co-founder <a href="/wiki/Ben_Chestnut" title="Ben Chestnut">Ben Chestnut</a> switched it around. He told Inc magazine that his parents had had "a pet monkey in Thailand. And they always warned me never to have a pet monkey. So I had this mischievous monkey in my brain."<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mal%C3%A9v" class="mw-redirect" title="Malév">Malév</a> – Hungary's national airline carrier. Its name comes from <b>Ma</b>gyar <b>Lé</b>giközlekedési <b>V</b>állalat – meaning Hungarian Air-traffic Company.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/MAN_SE" title="MAN SE">MAN</a> – abbreviation for <b>M</b>aschinenfabrik <b>A</b>ugsburg-<b>N</b>ürnberg (Augsburg-Nuremberg Machine Company). The MAN company is a German engineering works and truck manufacturer.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mandriva" title="Mandriva">Mandriva</a> – new company formed from the merger of <b>Mandr</b>ake Linux and Connect<b>iva</b> Linux</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Manugistics" title="Manugistics">Manugistics</a> – <b>Manu</b>facturing + Lo<b>gistics</b>, a supplier of supply chain optimization software</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Manulife_Financial" class="mw-redirect" title="Manulife Financial">Manulife Financial</a> – founded in 1887 as <b>Manu</b>facturing <b>Life</b> Insurance Company</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mars,_Incorporated" title="Mars, Incorporated">Mars</a> – named after Frank C. Mars and his wife, Ethel, who started making candy in 1911. Their son, Forrest E. Mars, joined with Bruce Murrie, the son of a Hershey executive, to form <a href="/wiki/M%26M%27s" title="M&amp;M's">M&amp;M Ltd</a> (from <b>M</b>ars &amp; <b>M</b>urrie). Forrest took over the family business after his father's death and merged the two companies in 1964. After retiring from Mars, Inc. in 1993, Forrest founded Ethel M. Chocolates, named after his mother.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Masco_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Masco Corporation">Masco Corporation</a> – from the names of the founder Alex <b>Ma</b>noogian, <b>S</b>crew and <b>Co</b>mpany. Masco Screw Products Co. was founded in 1929.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mast-J%C3%A4germeister_AG" class="mw-redirect" title="Mast-Jägermeister AG">Mast-Jägermeister AG</a> – named for founder Wilhelm Mast and its main product, <a href="/wiki/J%C3%A4germeister" title="Jägermeister">Jägermeister</a> (German for "hunt master") liqueur</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mattel" title="Mattel">Mattel</a> – <a href="/wiki/Portmanteau" title="Portmanteau">portmanteau</a> of the founders names Harold "Matt" Matson and Elliot Handler</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Maybach-Motorenbau_GmbH" class="mw-redirect" title="Maybach-Motorenbau GmbH">Maybach-Motorenbau GmbH</a> – German for "Maybach Engine Construction Company" – was named after <a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_Maybach" title="Wilhelm Maybach">Wilhelm Maybach</a> and his son Karl Maybach, who founded it in 1909. The Maybach name continued as a brand of <a href="/wiki/Daimler_AG" title="Daimler AG">Daimler AG</a> until the end of 2012.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mazda" title="Mazda">Mazda Motor Corporation</a> – company was founded as Toyo Kogyo, started manufacturing Mazda brand cars in 1931, and changed its name to Mazda in 1984. The cars were supposedly named after <a href="/wiki/Ahura_Mazda" title="Ahura Mazda">Ahura Mazda</a>, the chief deity of the Zoroastrians, though many think this explanation was created after the fact, to cover up what is simply a poor anglicized version of the founders name, Jujiro Matsuda.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/MBNA" title="MBNA">MBNA</a> – originally a subsidiary of Maryland National Corporation, MBNA once stood for <b>M</b>aryland <b>B</b>ank, <b>NA</b> (NA itself standing for National Association, a federal designation representing the bank's charter).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s" title="McDonald's">McDonald's</a> – from the name of the brothers <a href="/wiki/Dick_McDonald" class="mw-redirect" title="Dick McDonald">Dick McDonald</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dick_and_Mac_McDonald" class="mw-redirect" title="Dick and Mac McDonald">Mac McDonald</a>, who founded the first McDonald's restaurant in 1940.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/MCI_Communications" title="MCI Communications">MCI Communications</a> – <b>M</b>icrowave <b>C</b>ommunications, <b>I</b>nc. The company later merged with <a href="/wiki/Worldcom" class="mw-redirect" title="Worldcom">Worldcom</a> to create <a href="/wiki/MCI_Worldcom" class="mw-redirect" title="MCI Worldcom">MCI Worldcom</a>. The MCI was dropped in 2000 and the acquiring company changed its name to MCI when it emerged from bankruptcy in 2003.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/McSweeney%27s" title="McSweeney's">McSweeney's</a> – <a href="/wiki/Dave_Eggers" title="Dave Eggers">Dave Eggers</a>' publishing ventures started with <i><a href="/wiki/Timothy_McSweeney%27s_Quarterly_Concern" title="Timothy McSweeney's Quarterly Concern">Timothy McSweeney's Quarterly Concern</a></i>. This was named after mysterious letters that he collected as a child, "written by a man named Timothy McSweeney, who thought he was related to my mother".<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> (McSweeney was his mother's maiden name.)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz" title="Mercedes-Benz">Mercedes-Benz</a> – formed from the first name of <a href="/wiki/Merc%C3%A9d%C3%A8s_Jellinek" title="Mercédès Jellinek">Mercédès Jellinek</a>, the daughter of <a href="/wiki/Emil_Jellinek" title="Emil Jellinek">Emil Jellinek</a>, who distributed cars of the early Daimler company around 1900, and the last name of <a href="/wiki/Karl_Benz" title="Karl Benz">Karl Benz</a>, one of the owners of the <a href="/wiki/Daimler-Benz" class="mw-redirect" title="Daimler-Benz">Daimler-Benz</a> company that the Daimler company merged into in 1926.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Merillat_Industries" title="Merillat Industries">Merillat Industries</a> – named after <a href="/wiki/Orville_D._Merillat" title="Orville D. Merillat">Orville D. Merillat</a>, who founded the company in 1946.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer" title="Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer">Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer</a> (MGM) – film studio formed from the merger of three other companies: <b>Metro</b> Picture Corporation, <a href="/wiki/Goldwyn_Pictures_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Goldwyn Pictures Corporation"><b>Goldwyn</b> Pictures Corporation</a>, and Louis B. <b>Mayer</b> Pictures. Goldwyn Picture Corporation in turn was named after the last names of <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Goldwyn" title="Samuel Goldwyn">Samuel Goldfish</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Edgar_Selwyn" title="Edgar Selwyn">Edgar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Archibald_Selwyn" title="Archibald Selwyn">Archibald Selwyn</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/MFI_Retail" class="mw-redirect" title="MFI Retail">MFI</a> – from <b>M</b>ullard <b>F</b>urniture <b>I</b>ndustries. The original company was named after the founder's wife, whose maiden name was Mullard.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/MG_Cars" title="MG Cars">MG Cars</a> – from <b>M</b>orris <b>G</b>arages after co-founder William Morris. Under Chinese ownership, the company says: "We want Chinese consumers to know this brand as 'Modern Gentleman'."<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Microlins" title="Microlins">Microlins</a> – from <b>Micro</b>computers and <a href="/wiki/Lins,_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Lins, São Paulo">Lins</a>, a Brazilian city where the company was founded by <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Carlos_Semenzato" title="José Carlos Semenzato">José Carlos Semenzato</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Micron_Technology" title="Micron Technology">Micron Technology</a> – computer memory producer named after the microscopic parts of its products. It is now better known by its consumer brand name: Crucial.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> – coined by Bill Gates to represent the company that was devoted to <b>micro</b>computer <b>soft</b>ware. Originally christened Micro-Soft, the '-' disappeared on 3/2/1987 with the introduction of a new corporate identity and logo. The "slash between the 'o' and 's' [in the Microsoft logo] emphasizes the "soft" part of the name and conveys motion and speed."<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2007)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Midway_Games" title="Midway Games">Midway Games</a> – derived from the name of an airport on the southwestern part of Chicago.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Miele" title="Miele">Miele</a> – German based manufacturer of high-end domestic appliances, founded in 1899 by <a href="/wiki/Carl_Miele" title="Carl Miele">Carl Miele</a> and Reinhard Zinkann.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mincom_Limited" class="mw-redirect" title="Mincom Limited">Mincom Limited</a> – company initially created software to specifically assist mining companies and the name <b>Min</b>ing '<i><b>com</b>puting.</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Minolta" title="Minolta">Minolta</a> – founded in Osaka, Japan in 1928 as Nichi-Doku Shashinki Shōten (日独写真機商店; literally: Japan-Germany camera shop). It was not until 1934 that the name Minolta first appeared on a camera, the Minolta Vest. The name was given by founder Kazuo Tajima due to its similarity to the Japanese term "minoru ta" {稔る田} meaning "growing rice fields", which came from an ancient Japanese proverb that was a favorite of Tajima's mother meaning "the ripest ears of rice bow their heads lowest", and a desire from Tajima to run an innovative, yet humble business.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/MIPRO" title="MIPRO">MIPRO</a> – stands for <b>MI</b>crophone <b>PRO</b>fessionals. MIPRO is a manufacturer of wireless microphones.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/MIPS_Technologies" title="MIPS Technologies">MIPS</a> – originally stood for <b>M</b>icroprocessor without <b>I</b>nterlocking <b>P</b>ipeline <b>S</b>tages. When interlocks where added to a later implementation, the name was redefined to not be an acronym but just a name. (The name also connotes computer speed, by association with the acronym for <b>m</b>illions of <b>i</b>nstructions <b>p</b>er <b>s</b>econd.)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/MITIE" class="mw-redirect" title="MITIE">MITIE</a> – acronym for Management Incentive Through Investment Equity</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mitel" title="Mitel">Mitel</a> – from <b>Mi</b>ke and <b>Te</b>rry's <b>L</b>awnmowers, after the founders Michael Cowpland (see also: Corel) and Terry Matthews, and the company's original business plan</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/MITRE" class="mw-redirect" title="MITRE">MITRE</a> – <b>M</b>assachusetts <b>I</b>nstitute of <b>T</b>echnology <b>R</b>esearch <b>E</b>stablishment<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> (however, the MITRE Corporation asserts that its name is not an acronym<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mitsubishi" title="Mitsubishi">Mitsubishi</a> – name Mitsubishi (三菱) has two parts: mitsu means three and hishi (changing to bishi in the middle of the word) means diamond (the shape). Hence, the three diamond logo. (Note that "diamond" in this context refers only to the rhombus shape, not to the precious gem.)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mondelez_International" title="Mondelez International">Mondelez International</a> - American multinational snacks company spun off from <a href="/wiki/Kraft_Foods_Inc" class="mw-redirect" title="Kraft Foods Inc">Kraft Foods Inc</a>. Kraft Foods said: "'Monde' derives from the Latin word for 'world,' and 'delez' is a fanciful expression of 'delicious'. In addition, 'International' captures the global nature of the business."<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Moneris_Solutions" title="Moneris Solutions">Moneris Solutions</a> – Latin for "you <i>(singular)</i> are being protected"<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Morningstar,_Inc." title="Morningstar, Inc.">Morningstar, Inc.</a> – name is taken from the last sentence in <i>Walden</i>, a book by Henry David Thoreau; "the sun is but a morning star"</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Motorola" title="Motorola">Motorola</a> – founded in 1928 as the Galvin Manufacturing Company by two brothers, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Galvin_(businessman)" title="Paul Galvin (businessman)">Paul V.</a> and Joseph E. Galvin. It was renamed after its Motorola car radios became widely known. The "ola" ending was already in use, most famously for the "Victrola" phonograph made by the Victor Talking Machine Company.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mozilla_Foundation" title="Mozilla Foundation">Mozilla Foundation</a> – from the name of the web browser that preceded <a href="/wiki/Netscape_Navigator" title="Netscape Navigator">Netscape Navigator</a>. When Marc Andreesen, co-founder of <a href="/wiki/Netscape_Communications_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Netscape Communications Corporation">Netscape</a>, created a browser to replace the Mosaic browser, it was internally named Mozilla (Mosaic-Killer, <a href="/wiki/Godzilla" title="Godzilla">Godzilla</a>) by <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Zawinski" title="Jamie Zawinski">Jamie Zawinski</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mozy" title="Mozy">Mozy</a> – from the words "<b>Mo</b>re <b>Z</b>etabytes for <b>Y</b>our Mom". It was initially named "Breakaway Data Services for Your Mom," or "Bdsym".</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Madras_Rubber_Factory" class="mw-redirect" title="Madras Rubber Factory">MRF</a> – from <b>M</b>adras <b>R</b>ubber <b>F</b>actory, founded by K M Mammen Mappillai in 1946. He started with a toy-balloon manufacturing unit at Tiruvottiyur, Chennai (then called Madras). In 1952 he began manufacturing tread-rubber and, in 1961, tyres.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/MTM_Enterprises" title="MTM Enterprises">MTM Enterprises</a> – from the initials of the co-founder, actress <a href="/wiki/Mary_Tyler_Moore" title="Mary Tyler Moore">Mary Tyler Moore</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Musco_Lighting" title="Musco Lighting">Musco Lighting</a> – from the company's original location of <a href="/wiki/Muscatine_County,_Iowa" title="Muscatine County, Iowa"><b>Mus</b>catine <b>Co</b>unty, Iowa</a>, where it still operates a large manufacturing facility</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mustek_Systems" title="Mustek Systems">Mustek</a> –  Taiwanese electronics manufacturer with name derived from <b>M</b>ost <b>U</b>nique <b>S</b>canner <b>Tech</b>nology</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Music_and_Video_Club" title="Music and Video Club">MVC</a> – from <b>M</b>usic and <b>V</b>ideo <b>C</b>lub, the name of a UK-based entertainment chain</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="N">N</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_company_name_etymologies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: N">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Nabisco" title="Nabisco">Nabisco</a> – The <b>Na</b>tional <b>Bis</b>cuit <b>Co</b>mpany changed its name to Nabisco in 1971.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/NAD_Electronics" title="NAD Electronics">NAD Electronics</a> – audio equipment manufacturer named for <b>N</b>ew <b>A</b>coustic <b>D</b>imension</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Napster" title="Napster">Napster</a> – original music-sharing service was named after co-founder <a href="/wiki/Shawn_Fanning" title="Shawn Fanning">Shawn Fanning</a>'s hairstyle-based nickname</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/NCR_Corporation" title="NCR Corporation">NCR Corporation</a> – from <b>N</b>ational <b>C</b>ash <b>R</b>egister</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/NEC" title="NEC">NEC</a> – from <b>N</b>ippon <b>E</b>lectric <b>C</b>ompany</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nero_AG" title="Nero AG">Nero</a> – <a href="/wiki/Nero_Burning_ROM" title="Nero Burning ROM">Nero Burning ROM</a> named after <i>Nero burning Rome</i> ("Rom" is the German spelling of "Rome").</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nestl%C3%A9" title="Nestlé">Nestlé</a> – named after its founder, <a href="/wiki/Henri_Nestl%C3%A9" title="Henri Nestlé">Henri Nestlé</a>, who was born in Germany under the name "Nestle", which is German (actually, Swabian <a href="/wiki/Diminutive" title="Diminutive">diminutive</a>) for "bird's nest". The company logo is a bird's nest with a mother bird and two chicks.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Netscape" title="Netscape">Netscape</a> – originally the product name of the company's web browser ("Mosaic Communications <i>Netscape</i> Web Navigator"). The company adopted the product name after the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Illinois_at_Urbana%E2%80%93Champaign" title="University of Illinois at Urbana–Champaign">University of Illinois</a> threatened to sue for trademark infringement over the use of the Mosaic name. Netscape is the combination of network and landscape.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nike,_Inc." title="Nike, Inc.">Nike</a> – named for the <a href="/wiki/Nike_(mythology)" title="Nike (mythology)">Greek goddess of victory</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nikon" title="Nikon">Nikon</a> – original name was <b>Ni</b>ppon <b>Ko</b>gaku, meaning "Japanese Optical"</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nintendo" title="Nintendo">Nintendo</a> – Nintendo is the transliteration of the company's Japanese name, <i>nintendou</i> (任天堂). The first (<i>nin</i>) can be translated as to "entrusted"; <i>ten-dou</i> means "heaven".</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nissan_Motors" class="mw-redirect" title="Nissan Motors">Nissan</a> – earlier known by the name <b>Ni</b>ppon <b>San</b>gyo, which means "Japan Industries"</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nokia" title="Nokia">Nokia</a> – started as a wood-pulp mill, the company expanded into producing rubber products in the Finnish town of <a href="/wiki/Nokia,_Finland" title="Nokia, Finland">Nokia</a>. The company later adopted the town's name.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nortel" title="Nortel">Nortel Networks</a> – named from Nortel (<b>Nor</b>thern <b>Tel</b>ecom) and Bay <b>Networks</b>. The company was originally spun off from the Bell Telephone Company of Canada Ltd in 1895 as Northern Electric and Manufacturing, and traded as Northern Electric from 1914 to 1976.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Novartis" title="Novartis">Novartis</a> – after the Latin expression "novae artes" which means something like "new skills"</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Novell" title="Novell">Novell</a> – Novell, Inc. was earlier <a href="/wiki/Novell_Data_Systems" class="mw-redirect" title="Novell Data Systems">Novell Data Systems</a> co-founded by George Canova. The name was suggested by George's wife who mistakenly thought that "Novell" meant <i>new</i> in French. (Nouvelle is the feminine form of the French adjective 'Nouveau'. Nouvelle as a noun in French is 'news'.)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nvidia" title="Nvidia">Nvidia</a> (stylized as NVIDIA) – comes from "<a href="/wiki/Invidia" title="Invidia">invidia</a>" in <a href="/wiki/Roman_mythology" title="Roman mythology">Roman mythology</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> word for "<a href="/wiki/Envy" title="Envy">envy</a>".</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="O">O</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_company_name_etymologies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: O">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/OCZ_Technology" class="mw-redirect" title="OCZ Technology">OCZ</a> – play on the word <b>O</b>ver<b>c</b>locker<b>s</b><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Olympus_Corporation" title="Olympus Corporation">Olympus</a> – Japanese company founded as Takachiho Seisakusho in 1919, where Takachiho referred to <a href="/wiki/Takama-ga-hara" class="mw-redirect" title="Takama-ga-hara">Takama-ga-hara</a>, the home of the gods in <a href="/wiki/Japanese_mythology" title="Japanese mythology">Japanese mythology</a>. It was renamed Olympus Optical Co., Ltd in 1949, after <a href="/wiki/Mount_Olympus" title="Mount Olympus">Mount Olympus</a>, the home of the gods in <a href="/wiki/Greek_mythology" title="Greek mythology">Greek mythology</a>, and then Olympus Corporation in 2003. The company had been using Olympus as a brand name for optical products such as microscopes since 1921.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Onkyo" title="Onkyo">Onkyo</a> – translates as "sound harmony". The Japanese audio company was founded as Osaka Denki Onkyo K.K in 1946.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ooyala" title="Ooyala">Ooyala</a> – word Ooyala (ఉయ్యల) means 'cradle' in <a href="/wiki/Telugu_language" title="Telugu language">Telugu</a>, as in a "cradle of innovation".</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Oracle_Corporation" title="Oracle Corporation">Oracle</a> – Larry Ellison, Ed Oates and Bob Miner worked on a consulting project, code-named Oracle, for the <a href="/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency" title="Central Intelligence Agency">CIA</a>. The project was designed to use the new SQL database language from IBM. When the project was terminated, they decided to finish what they started and market it. Later they changed the name of their company, Relational Software Inc., to the name of the product.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ornge_(Ontario_Air_Ambulance)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ornge (Ontario Air Ambulance)">Ornge</a> – new name (2006) for <a href="/wiki/Ontario_Air_Ambulance" class="mw-redirect" title="Ontario Air Ambulance">Ontario Air Ambulance</a>, chosen to reflect the orange color of its aircraft. It was intended to provide a unique branding but the ornge.com misspelling was already used by an advertising portal.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Osram" title="Osram">Osram</a> – from <a href="/wiki/Osmium" title="Osmium"><b>os</b>mium</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tungsten" title="Tungsten">wolf<b>ram</b></a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/%C3%96ssur" title="Össur">Össur</a> – from the name of the founder, Icelandic entrepreneur Össur Kristinsson</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="P">P</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_company_name_etymologies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: P">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Paccar" title="Paccar">Paccar</a> – from <b>Pac</b>ific <b>C</b>ar <b>a</b>nd <b>R</b>ail</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/PCCW" title="PCCW">PCCW</a> – originally Pacific Century Development, the company's English name was changed from <b>P</b>acific <b>C</b>entury <b>C</b>yber<b>W</b>orks Limited to PCCW Limited on 9 August 2002. It owns Hong Kong Telecom.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pamida" title="Pamida">Pamida</a> – U.S. retailer co-founded by <a href="/wiki/Jim_Witherspoon" title="Jim Witherspoon">Jim Witherspoon</a> and named after his three sons: <b>Pa</b>trick, <b>Mi</b>chael and <b>Da</b>vid. Following a merger in 2012, Pamida's 175 stores were rebranded as <a href="/wiki/Shopko" title="Shopko">Shopko</a> Hometown stores or closed.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Panasonic" title="Panasonic">Panasonic</a> – the giant Japanese electronics manufacturer was originally called Matsushita, after its founder, <a href="/wiki/K%C5%8Dnosuke_Matsushita" title="Kōnosuke Matsushita">Kōnosuke Matsushita</a>. In 2008, it was renamed Panasonic Corporation after the brand names it used for TV sales in the United States. National, its original global brand name, was not available in the United States and was abandoned.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pemex" title="Pemex">Pemex</a> – abbreviation of the full name of the state-owned Mexican oil/gasoline company, <b>Pe</b>tróleos <b>Mex</b>icanos (Spanish for <i>Mexican Petroleum</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pennzoil" title="Pennzoil">Pennzoil</a> – formed by a merger of South Penn Oil (<b>Penn</b>), a former <a href="/wiki/Standard_Oil" title="Standard Oil">Standard Oil</a> subsidiary, and <a href="/wiki/Zapata_Oil" class="mw-redirect" title="Zapata Oil">Zapata Oil</a> (<b>zoil</b>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Penske_Corporation" title="Penske Corporation">Penske Corporation</a> – transportation company founded in 1969 by US racing driver <a href="/wiki/Roger_Penske" title="Roger Penske">Roger Penske</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pepsi" title="Pepsi">Pepsi</a> – named from the digestive enzyme <a href="/wiki/Pepsin" title="Pepsin">pepsin</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pernod_Ricard" title="Pernod Ricard">Pernod Ricard</a> – French drinks company formed in 1975 with the merger of eponymous rivals founded by Henri-Louis Pernod and <a href="/wiki/Paul_Ricard" title="Paul Ricard">Paul Ricard</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Petrobras" title="Petrobras">Petrobras</a> – abbreviation of the <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazilian</a> <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">oil</a> company's full name, <b>Petró</b>leo <b>Bras</b>ileiro (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> for <i>Brazilian Petroleum</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Peugeot" title="Peugeot">Peugeot</a> – in 1810, Jean-Pierre and Jean-Frédéric Peugeot diversified their family-run grain mill into a steel foundry. In 1896, after a family squabble, <a href="/wiki/Armand_Peugeot" title="Armand Peugeot">Armand Peugeot</a> founded the Société des Automobiles Peugeot to focus on cars.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pez" title="Pez">Pez</a> – from the first, middle and last letters of the <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German language</a> word "<b>P</b>feff<b>e</b>rmin<b>z</b>", meaning "<a href="/wiki/Peppermint" title="Peppermint">peppermint</a>"<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Philco" title="Philco">Philco</a> – from the <b>Phil</b>adelphia Storage Battery <b>Co</b>mpany. The pioneering U.S. radio and television manufacturer was taken over by <a href="/wiki/Ford" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford">Ford</a> and later by <a href="/wiki/Philips" title="Philips">Philips</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Philips" title="Philips">Philips</a> – Royal Philips Electronics was founded in 1891 by brothers Gerard (the engineer) and Anton (the entrepreneur) Philips</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Piaggio" title="Piaggio">Piaggio</a> – Italian manufacturer of Vespa scooters and cars was named after its founder, Rinaldo Piaggio.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pioneer_Corporation" title="Pioneer Corporation">Pioneer Corporation</a> – In 1938, <a href="/wiki/Nozomu_Matsumoto" title="Nozomu Matsumoto">Nozomu Matsumoto</a>, the son of a Christian missionary, founded Fukuin Shokai Denki Seisakusho ("Gospel Electric Works") to manufacture the A-8 loudspeaker, which he called "Pioneer". The company name was changed to the religiously neutral Pioneer Electronic Corporation in 1961, when it went public. In 1999, the company simplified its name by removing "Electronic".<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pixar" title="Pixar">Pixar</a> – from <b>pix</b>el and the co-founder's name, <b>A</b>lvy <b>R</b>ay Smith. According to the biography "The Second Coming of Steve Jobs" by Alan Deutschman, the 'el' in pixel was changed to 'ar' because 'ar' is frequently used in Spanish verbs, implying the name means "To Pix". Alternatively, "pixarr" is a common abbreviation for "pixel array," an often used term in computer graphics programming.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/PMC-Sierra" title="PMC-Sierra">PMC-Sierra</a> – PMC from <b>P</b>acific <b>M</b>icroelectronics <b>C</b>entre, a research arm of BC Tel, and Sierra from the company that acquired it, Sierra Semiconductor, presumably so named because of the allure of the Sierra Nevada mountains to members of a California-based company.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Porsche" title="Porsche">Porsche</a> – car company named after founder <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Porsche" title="Ferdinand Porsche">Ferdinand Porsche</a>, an Austrian automotive engineer. The family name may have originated in the Czech name "Boreš" (boresh).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/POW!_Entertainment" title="POW! Entertainment">POW! Entertainment</a> – American media production company co-founded by former <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Comics" title="Marvel Comics">Marvel Comics</a> editor and publisher <a href="/wiki/Stan_Lee" title="Stan Lee">Stan Lee</a> in 2001. POW! is commonly used in comic book fights, but it is used as an acroynm (or backronym) in the name POW! (Purveyors of Wonder) Entertainment, Inc.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Prada" title="Prada">Prada</a> – an Italian high fashion house named after the founder Mario <b>Prada</b>, who founded <a href="/wiki/Prada" title="Prada">Prada</a> in Milan 1914</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/PricewaterhouseCoopers" title="PricewaterhouseCoopers">PricewaterhouseCoopers</a> – global professional services firm named as a result of the merger of Price Waterhouse and Coopers &amp; Lybrand in 1998. It started trading as PwC in 2010 without changing its legal name.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Procter_%26_Gamble" title="Procter &amp; Gamble">Procter &amp; Gamble</a> – named after the founders, William Procter, a candlemaker, and James Gamble, a soapmaker, who pooled their resources after marrying two sisters. The company was founded in Cincinnati in 1837.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/ProfSat" title="ProfSat">ProfSat</a> – Brazilian <a href="/wiki/Satellite" title="Satellite">satellite</a>-based education company, meaning <b>Prof</b>essional <b>Sat</b>eliite</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Proton_(carmaker)" class="mw-redirect" title="Proton (carmaker)">Proton</a> – the Malaysian car manufacturer's name is derived from <b>P</b>e<b>r</b>usahaan <b>Oto</b>mobil <b>N</b>asional, which means <i>National Automobile Enterprise</i> in the <a href="/wiki/Malay_language" title="Malay language">Malay</a> language.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/PRS_Guitars" title="PRS Guitars">PRS Guitars</a> – named after its founder, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Reed_Smith" title="Paul Reed Smith">Paul Reed Smith</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Psion_(computers)" class="mw-redirect" title="Psion (computers)">Psion</a> – UK computer company named by its founder, South Africa-born Dr David Potter, from <b>P</b>otter <b>S</b>cientific <b>I</b>nstruments <b>O</b>r <b>N</b>othing</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Q">Q</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_company_name_etymologies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Q">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Kuwait_Petroleum_International" title="Kuwait Petroleum International">Q8</a> – acronym for these gas stations sounds like <i>Kuwait</i>, that is, the letter Q followed by the number 8. It is the abbreviation for <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_Petroleum_International_Limited" class="mw-redirect" title="Kuwait Petroleum International Limited">Kuwait Petroleum International Limited</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Qantas" title="Qantas">Qantas</a> – from its original name, <b>Q</b>ueensland <b>a</b>nd <b>N</b>orthern <b>T</b>erritory <b>A</b>erial <b>S</b>ervices</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Qimonda" title="Qimonda">Qimonda</a> – invented name, where the company says: "In Chinese, 'Qi', pronounced as 'ch-ee', stands for breathing and flowing energy, while 'monda' denotes 'world' in Latin-based languages. 'Qi', when pronounced as a hard 'k', suggests 'key to the world', a positive connotation." It filed for insolvency on January 23, 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Quad_Electroacoustics" title="Quad Electroacoustics">Quad</a> – acronym for <b>Q</b>uality <b>U</b>nit <b>A</b>mplified <b>D</b>omestic. Quad Electroacoustics was founded in 1936 by Peter Walker, and was formerly called the Acoustical Manufacturing Company.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Quark,_Inc." class="mw-redirect" title="Quark, Inc.">Quark</a> – named after the subatomic particle. The word <i><a href="/wiki/Quark" title="Quark">quark</a></i> originates from <a href="/wiki/Finnegans_Wake" title="Finnegans Wake">Finnegans Wake</a> by <a href="/wiki/James_Joyce" title="James Joyce">James Joyce</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Qualcomm" title="Qualcomm">Qualcomm</a> – <b>Qual</b>ity <b>Comm</b>unication</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Quora" title="Quora">Quora</a> – faux plural of <i><a href="/wiki/Quorum" title="Quorum">quorum</a></i>, evocative of questions and answers<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/QVC" title="QVC">QVC</a> – <b>Q</b>uality, <b>V</b>alue and <b>C</b>onvenience</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="R">R</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_company_name_etymologies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: R">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Rabobank" title="Rabobank">Rabobank</a> – <b>Ra</b>iffeisen-<b>Bo</b>erenleen<b>bank</b> (Dutch for "Farmers Loan Bank"), a combination of the two cooperatives that merged to form the company</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Raising_Cane%27s_Chicken_Fingers" title="Raising Cane's Chicken Fingers">Raising Cane's Chicken Fingers</a> – from "Raising Cane", a Labrador Retriever owned by chain founder Todd Graves when he opened his first restaurant in 1996<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/RAND_Corporation" title="RAND Corporation">RAND</a> – <b>R</b>esearch <b>AN</b>d <b>D</b>evelopment.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Raytheon" title="Raytheon">Raytheon</a> – "light of the gods"; maker of missiles such as Patriot, Maverick, Sidewinder and Tomahawk, among other military technology</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/RCA" title="RCA">RCA</a> – <b>R</b>adio <b>C</b>orporation of <b>A</b>merica</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Reckitt_%26_Colman" class="mw-redirect" title="Reckitt &amp; Colman">Reckitt &amp; Colman</a> – named from the merger of Reckitt &amp; Sons with J&amp;J Colman in 1938. <a href="/wiki/Colman%27s" title="Colman's">Colman's</a>, best known for its mustard, was founded by <a href="/wiki/Jeremiah_Colman" title="Jeremiah Colman">Jeremiah Colman</a> in 1814. <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Reckitt" title="Isaac Reckitt">Isaac Reckitt</a> founded Reckitt &amp; Sons in 1840.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Reckitt_Benckiser" title="Reckitt Benckiser">Reckitt Benckiser</a> – consumer goods giant named from the merger of Britain's <a href="/wiki/Reckitt_%26_Colman" class="mw-redirect" title="Reckitt &amp; Colman">Reckitt &amp; Colman</a> and the Dutch company Benckiser NV in December 1999. The latter was named after its founder, <a href="/wiki/Johann_Benckiser" title="Johann Benckiser">Johann Benckiser</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Red_Hat" title="Red Hat">Red Hat</a> – while at college, company founder Marc Ewing was given the <a href="/wiki/Cornell_University" title="Cornell University">Cornell</a> <a href="/wiki/Lacrosse" title="Lacrosse">lacrosse</a> team cap (with red and white stripes) by his grandfather. People would turn to him to solve their problems and he was referred to as "that guy in the red hat". By the time he wrote the manual of the beta version of Red Hat Linux he had lost the cap, so the manual included an appeal to readers to return his <i>Red Hat</i> if found.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Reebok" title="Reebok">Reebok</a> – alternate spelling of <a href="/wiki/Rhebok" class="mw-redirect" title="Rhebok">rhebok</a> (Pelea capreolus), an African antelope</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Renault" title="Renault">Renault</a> – French car manufacturer founded in 1899 as Société Renault Frères (French for <i>Renault Brothers</i>) by <a href="/wiki/Louis_Renault_(industrialist)" title="Louis Renault (industrialist)">Louis Renault</a> and his brothers Marcel and Fernand.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/REO_Motor_Car_Company" title="REO Motor Car Company">REO Motor Car Company</a> – car manufacturer founded in 1904 by <a href="/wiki/Ransom_E._Olds" title="Ransom E. Olds">Ransom E. Olds</a>, and named from its founder's initials. Later, the rock band <a href="/wiki/REO_Speedwagon" title="REO Speedwagon">REO Speedwagon</a> took its name from one of its trucks, the <a href="/wiki/REO_Speed_Wagon" title="REO Speed Wagon">REO Speed Wagon</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Repsol_YPF" class="mw-redirect" title="Repsol YPF">Repsol</a> – name derived from <b>Re</b>finería de <b>P</b>etróleo de e<b>S</b>combreras <b>O</b>i<b>l</b> (Escombreras is an oil refinery in Cartagena, Spain) and chosen for its euphony when the, then, state-owned oil company was incorporated in 1986. Previously Repsol was a lubricating-oil trademark.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/BlackBerry_Limited" title="BlackBerry Limited">Research in Motion</a> – from the phrase "poetry in motion", which company founder <a href="/wiki/Mike_Lazaridis" title="Mike Lazaridis">Mike Lazaridis</a> had seen used to describe a <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">football</a> player. The company changed its name to BlackBerry in 2013, after <a href="/wiki/BlackBerry" title="BlackBerry">its most famous product</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rickenbacker" title="Rickenbacker">Rickenbacker</a> – named after co-founder <a href="/wiki/Adolph_Rickenbacher" class="mw-redirect" title="Adolph Rickenbacher">Adolph Rickenbacher</a>, with the spelling anglicised. The company started as the Electro String Instrument Corporation in 1931.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rio_Tinto_(corporation)" title="Rio Tinto (corporation)">Rio Tinto</a> - the Anglo-Australian multinational mining company’s name comes from the <a href="/wiki/Rio_Tinto_(river)" title="Rio Tinto (river)">Rio Tinto</a> (Red River) in southwestern Spain, which has flowed red since mining began there about 5000 years ago, due to <a href="/wiki/Acid_mine_drainage" title="Acid mine drainage">acid mine drainage</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Robeez" title="Robeez">Robeez</a> – baby-shoe company named after the founder's son Robbie (Robert)<sup id="cite_ref-Robeez_Footwear:_Better_By_Design_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Robeez_Footwear:_Better_By_Design-105">[105]</a></sup> Robeez was taken over by <a href="/wiki/Stride_Rite" class="mw-redirect" title="Stride Rite">Stride Rite</a> in 2006.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hoffmann-La_Roche" title="Hoffmann-La Roche">Roche</a> – healthcare company named after its founder, <a href="/wiki/Fritz_Hoffmann-La_Roche" title="Fritz Hoffmann-La Roche">Fritz Hoffmann-La Roche</a><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup>. The compound surname was the result of Fritz Hoffmann marrying Adèle La Roche in 1895: it was a common practice in Switzerland at that time.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Roku" title="Roku">Roku</a> – from the Japanese word <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E5%85%AD" class="extiw" title="wikt:六">六</a><span style="font-weight: normal"> (<span lang="ja">roku</span>)</span> meaning "six", because it was the sixth company started by <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Wood_(businessman)" title="Anthony Wood (businessman)">Anthony Wood</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rolls-Royce_Limited" title="Rolls-Royce Limited">Rolls-Royce</a> – name used by <a href="/wiki/Rolls-Royce_plc" class="mw-redirect" title="Rolls-Royce plc">Rolls-Royce plc</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rolls-Royce_Motor_Cars" title="Rolls-Royce Motor Cars">Rolls-Royce Motor Cars</a>, among others. In 1884 <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Henry_Royce" class="mw-redirect" title="Frederick Henry Royce">Frederick Henry Royce</a> started an electrical and mechanical business, making his first car, a <i>Royce</i>, in 1904. He was introduced to <a href="/wiki/Charles_Stewart_Rolls" class="mw-redirect" title="Charles Stewart Rolls">Charles Stewart Rolls</a> on 4 May that year. The pair entered into a partnership in which Royce would manufacture cars to be sold exclusively by Rolls, and the cars would be called <i>Rolls-Royce</i>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/ROLM" title="ROLM">ROLM</a> – named after the founders, Gene <b>R</b>icheson, Ken <b>O</b>shman, Walter <b>L</b>oewenstern, and Robert <b>M</b>axfield</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/RSA_Security" title="RSA Security">RSA Security</a> – formed from the first letters of the family names of its founders <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Rivest" class="mw-redirect" title="Ronald Rivest">Ronald Rivest</a>, <a href="/wiki/Adi_Shamir" title="Adi Shamir">Adi Shamir</a> and <a href="/wiki/Len_Adleman" class="mw-redirect" title="Len Adleman">Len Adleman</a></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="S">S</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_company_name_etymologies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: S">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Saab_Automobile" title="Saab Automobile">Saab</a> – founded in 1937 in <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a> as <i><b>S</b>venska <b>A</b>eroplan <a href="/wiki/Aktiebolag" title="Aktiebolag"><b>a</b>ktie<b>b</b>olaget</a></i> (Swedish Aeroplane Company); the last word is typically abbreviated as <b>AB</b>, hence Saab and Saab Automobile AB</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sabre_(computer_system)" title="Sabre (computer system)">Sabre</a> – <b>S</b>emi-<b>A</b>utomatic <b>B</b>usiness <b>R</b>esearch <b>E</b>nvironment</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Science_Applications_International_Corporation" title="Science Applications International Corporation">SAIC</a> – <b>S</b>cience <b>A</b>pplications <b>I</b>nternational <b>C</b>orporation</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/SAIC_Motor" title="SAIC Motor">SAIC Motor</a> – <b>S</b>hanghai <b>A</b>utomotive <b>I</b>ndustry <b>C</b>orporation</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Saku_Brewery" title="Saku Brewery">Saku Brewery</a> – after the <a href="/wiki/Saku,_Estonia" title="Saku, Estonia"><b>Saku</b></a> small borough, Estonia, where the company was founded</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Samsonite" title="Samsonite">Samsonite</a> – named from the Biblical character <a href="/wiki/Samson" title="Samson">Samson</a>, renowned for his strength</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sams_Publishing" title="Sams Publishing">Sams Publishing</a> – named after Howard W. Sams, who founded the company in 1946. It is now an imprint of <a href="/wiki/Pearson_PLC" class="mw-redirect" title="Pearson PLC">Pearson PLC</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Samsung_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Samsung Group">Samsung</a> – meaning "three stars" in Korean<sup id="cite_ref-Kim1996_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kim1996-109">[109]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Grupo_Santander" class="mw-redirect" title="Grupo Santander">Santander</a> – Banco Santander was founded in Spain in 1857 and named after the port of Santander in the north of Spain.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sanyo" title="Sanyo">Sanyo</a> – meaning "three oceans" in Japanese. The company was taken over by <a href="/wiki/Panasonic" title="Panasonic">Panasonic</a> in 2009 and the Sanyo brand name is no longer used.</li>
