<li><a href="/wiki/SAP_SE" title="SAP SE">SAP</a> – <i><b>S</b>ystem<b>A</b>nalyse und <b>P</b>rogrammentwicklung</i> (German for "System analysis and program development"), a company formed by five ex-IBM employees who used to work in the 'Systems/Applications/Projects' group of IBM. Later, SAP was redefined to stand for <i>Systeme, Anwendungen und Produkte in der Datenverarbeitung</i> (Systems, Applications and Products in Data Processing).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Scandinavian_Airlines_System" class="mw-redirect" title="Scandinavian Airlines System">SAS</a> – <b>S</b>candinavian <b>A</b>irlines <b>S</b>ystem, the flag airline carrier of <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>, Norway and <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/SAS_Institute" title="SAS Institute">SAS Institute</a> – originally an abbreviation for <b>S</b>tatistical <b>A</b>nalysis <b>S</b>ystem</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sasol" title="Sasol">Sasol</a> – <b>S</b>uid-<b>A</b>frikaanse <b>S</b>teenkool en <b>Ol</b>ie. (<a href="/wiki/Afrikaans" title="Afrikaans">Afrikaans</a> for <i>South African Coal and Oil</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Saudi_Aramco" title="Saudi Aramco">Saudi Aramco</a> – Aramco name was derived in 1944 when California Arabian Standard Oil Company (Casoc) changed its name to <b>Ar</b>abian <b>Am</b>erican Oil <b>Co</b>mpany. The Saudi government purchased the company in 1980, and changed its name to Saudi Arabian Oil Company or Saudi Aramco in 1988.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Selver" title="Selver">Selver</a> - from Estonian "<b>selve</b>hall" ("self-service market"), an earlier Estonian word for a "supermarket", and the noun suffix -<b>r</b>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Standard_Chartered_Bank" class="mw-redirect" title="Standard Chartered Bank">SCB</a> – from <b>S</b>tandard <b>C</b>hartered <b>B</b>ank. The name Standard Chartered comes from the two original banks from which it was founded – the Chartered Bank of Sri Lanka, Australia and China, and the Standard Bank of British South Africa.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Schick_(razors)" title="Schick (razors)">Schick</a> – manufacturer of shaving razors and blades, named after the inventor <a href="/wiki/Jacob_Schick" title="Jacob Schick">Jacob Schick</a><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_Operation" title="Santa Cruz Operation">SCO</a> – from <b>S</b>anta <b>C</b>ruz <b>O</b>peration. The company's office was in <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz,_California" title="Santa Cruz, California">Santa Cruz, California</a>. It eventually formed <a href="/wiki/Tarantella,_Inc." title="Tarantella, Inc.">Tarantella, Inc.</a> and sold off its operating system division to <a href="/wiki/Caldera_Systems" class="mw-redirect" title="Caldera Systems">Caldera Systems</a>, which is based in Utah. Caldera Systems changed its name to <a href="/wiki/Caldera_International" class="mw-redirect" title="Caldera International">Caldera International</a> and then to <a href="/wiki/The_SCO_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="The SCO Group">The SCO Group</a> (at which point SCO no longer stood for anything).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/SEAT" title="SEAT">SEAT</a> – an acronym from <b>S</b>ociedad <b>E</b>spañola de <b>A</b>utomóviles de <b>T</b>urismo (Spanish Corporation of Touring Cars)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sealed_Air" title="Sealed Air">Sealed Air</a> – from the "sealed air" found in its most notable product, Bubble Wrap</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sears" title="Sears">Sears, Roebuck</a> – named after its founders <a href="/wiki/Richard_Warren_Sears" title="Richard Warren Sears">Richard Warren Sears</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alvah_Curtis_Roebuck" title="Alvah Curtis Roebuck">Alvah Curtis Roebuck</a> in 1886, and taken over by <a href="/wiki/Kmart" title="Kmart">Kmart</a> in 2005. <a href="/wiki/Sears_Holdings" title="Sears Holdings">Sears Holdings</a> now owns both <a href="/wiki/Sears" title="Sears">Sears</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kmart" title="Kmart">Kmart</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sega" title="Sega">Sega</a> – <b>Se</b>rvice <b>Ga</b>mes of Japan was founded by Marty Bromley (an American) to import pinball games to Japan for use on American military bases.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Seiko" title="Seiko">Seiko</a> – Seiko, now referred to in <a href="/wiki/Katakana" title="Katakana">katakana</a> as セイコー("seiko"), was originally named in <a href="/wiki/Kanji" title="Kanji">kanji</a> as <b>精工</b>(also "seiko"). The two characters were taken from the phrase 「<b>精</b>巧で<b>精</b>密な時計の生産に成功する<b>工</b>場」, the company's vision which roughly translates to "a factory（工場:<b>ko</b>jyo）that successfully（成功:<b>seiko</b>）produces（生産:<b>sei</b>san）exquisit（精巧:<b>seiko</b>）and precise（精密:<b>sei</b>mitsu）watches". – According to Seiko's official company history, titled <i>A Journey in Time: The Remarkable Story of Seiko</i> (2003), Seiko is a Japanese word for "exquisite" or "minute" (both spelled 精巧), as well as a word for "success" (spelled 成功).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sennheiser" title="Sennheiser">Sennheiser</a> – named after one of its founders, <a href="/wiki/Fritz_Sennheiser" title="Fritz Sennheiser">Fritz Sennheiser</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Silicon_Graphics" title="Silicon Graphics">SGI</a> – <b>S</b>ilicon <b>G</b>raphics <b>I</b>nc.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sharp_Corporation" title="Sharp Corporation">Sharp</a> – Japanese consumer electronics company named from its first product, an ever-sharp pencil</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Royal_Dutch_Shell" title="Royal Dutch Shell">Shell</a> – Royal Dutch/Shell was established in 1907, when the Royal Dutch Petrol Society Plc. and the Shell Transport and Trading Company Ltd. merged their operations. The Shell Transport and Trading Company Ltd had been established at the end of the 19th century by commercial firm Samuel &amp; Co (founded in 1830). Samuel &amp; Co was already importing Japanese shells when it set up an oil company, so the oil company was named after the shells.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Siemens_AG" class="mw-redirect" title="Siemens AG">Siemens</a> – founded in 1847 by <a href="/wiki/Werner_von_Siemens" title="Werner von Siemens">Werner von Siemens</a> and Johann Georg Halske. The company was originally called <i>Telegraphen-Bau-Anstalt von Siemens &amp; Halske</i>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Six_Apart" title="Six Apart">Six Apart</a> – company co-founders <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Trott" title="Benjamin Trott">Ben</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mena_Grabowski_Trott" title="Mena Grabowski Trott">Mena</a> Trott were born six days apart in September 1977. In 2011, the company was taken over by Infocom, a Japanese IT company.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Skanska" title="Skanska">Skanska</a> – Swedish construction company named from Aktiebolaget Skånska Cementgjuteriet (<a href="/wiki/Scania" title="Scania">Scania</a> Cement Casting Ltd)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/SKF" title="SKF">SKF</a> – from <b>S</b>venska <b>K</b>ullager<b>f</b>abriken AB (<i>Swedish ball bearing factory</i>) founded in 1907; see also <a href="/wiki/Volvo" title="Volvo">Volvo</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Skoda_Auto" class="mw-redirect" title="Skoda Auto">Skoda Auto</a> – car company was founded in 1895 and originally named Laurin &amp; Klement after its founders, Vaclav Laurin and <a href="/wiki/Vaclav_Klement" class="mw-redirect" title="Vaclav Klement">Vaclav Klement</a>. It was taken over by <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0koda_Works" title="Škoda Works">Škoda Works</a>, an industrial conglomerate, in 1924, and adopted the Škoda name from <a href="/wiki/Emil_%C5%A0koda" title="Emil Škoda">Emil Škoda</a>. Škoda Auto was split off after World War II and is now part of <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen" title="Volkswagen">Volkswagen</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Skype" title="Skype">Skype</a> – original concept for the name was Sky-Peer-to-Peer, which morphed into Skyper, then Skype.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> The company was taken over by <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> in May 2011.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Smart_(marque)" title="Smart (marque)">Smart</a> – <b>S</b>watch + <b>M</b>ercedes + Art</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Smeg_(appliances)" title="Smeg (appliances)">Smeg</a>, <i><b>S</b>malterie <b>M</b>etallurgiche <b>E</b>miliane <b>G</b>uastalla</i> (metal enamelling of <a href="/wiki/Guastalla" title="Guastalla">Guastalla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emilia_(region_of_Italy)" title="Emilia (region of Italy)">Emilia</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Smilebit" title="Smilebit">Smilebit</a> – former Sega development studio named from what they hope to make you do (smile), and the smallest unit of computer information (bit). The company developed <a href="/wiki/Jet_Set_Radio" title="Jet Set Radio">Jet Set Radio</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/SNK_Playmore" class="mw-redirect" title="SNK Playmore">SNK</a> – <b>S</b>hin <b>N</b>ihon <b>K</b>ikaku, Japanese for "Plans for a New Japan"</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sony" title="Sony">Sony</a> – from the Latin word 'sonus' meaning sound, and 'sonny' a slang word used by Americans to refer to a bright youngster, "since we were sonny boys working in sound and vision", said Akio Morita. The company was founded as Tokyo Tsushin Kogyo KK (Tokyo Telecommunications Engineering Corporation) in 1946, and changed its name to Sony in 1958. Sony was chosen as it could be pronounced easily in many languages.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/SuperCalc" title="SuperCalc">Sorcim</a> – "Micros" backwards. Sorcim was the original publisher of the <a href="/wiki/SuperCalc" title="SuperCalc">SuperCalc</a> spreadsheet in 1980. It was taken over by <a href="/wiki/CA,_Inc." class="mw-redirect" title="CA, Inc.">Computer Associates</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/SPAR" class="mw-redirect" title="SPAR">SPAR</a> – originally DE SPAR, from <i><b>D</b>oor <b>E</b>endrachtig <b>S</b>amenwerken <b>P</b>rofiteren <b>A</b>llen <b>R</b>egelmatig</i> (Dutch, meaning "All will benefit from united co-operation"). "De spar" in Dutch translates as "the fir tree", hence the fir tree logo. As the company expanded across Europe, the name was shortened by dropping the article, "DE".</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sperry_Corporation" title="Sperry Corporation">Sperry</a> – company founded by <a href="/wiki/Elmer_Ambrose_Sperry" title="Elmer Ambrose Sperry">Elmer Ambrose Sperry</a> (1860–1930), originally as Sperry Gyroscope Company. Sperry took over Univac, and eventually was itself taken over by Burroughs. The merged companies became Unisys, from <b>Un</b>ited <b>I</b>nformation <b>Sys</b>tems.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Spiratone" title="Spiratone">Spiratone</a> – from the last name of founders <a href="/wiki/Fred_Spira" title="Fred Spira">Fred Spira</a> and Hans Spira. The company was founded as Spiratone Fine Grain Laboratories. The "tone" suffix was common in the photographic industry (an example cited by <a href="/wiki/Fred_Spira" title="Fred Spira">Fred Spira</a> is Royaltone) at the time of the company's founding in the 1940s.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sprint_Corporation" title="Sprint Corporation">Sprint</a> – from its parent company, <b>S</b>outhern <b>P</b>acific <b>R</b>ailroad <b>INT</b>ernal Communications. At the time, pipelines and railroad tracks were the cheapest place to lay communications lines, as the right-of-way was already leased or owned.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/SRAM_Corporation" title="SRAM Corporation">SRAM Corporation</a> – bicycle component manufacturer named from its founders <b>S</b>cott King, Stanley <b>R</b>ay Day, and S<b>am</b> Patterson</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/SRI_International" title="SRI International">SRI International</a> – from <b>S</b>tanford <b>R</b>esearch <b>I</b>nstitute, established by the trustees of <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford University</a>, California</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Stanley_Works" class="mw-redirect" title="Stanley Works">Stanley Works</a> – name created to reflect the merger of Stanley's Bolt Manufactory of New Britain, Connecticut (founded by <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Trent_Stanley" title="Frederick Trent Stanley">Frederick Trent Stanley</a>) and the Stanley Rule and Level Company (founded by his cousin Henry Stanley)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Starbucks" title="Starbucks">Starbucks</a> – named after Starbuck, a character in Herman Melville's novel <i><a href="/wiki/Moby-Dick" title="Moby-Dick">Moby-Dick</a></i>, also a variation of Starbo; at the time, a local mining camp north of Seattle.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Stellent" class="mw-redirect" title="Stellent">Stellent</a> – coined from a combination of the words <b>st</b>ellar and exc<b>ellent</b>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sturm,_Ruger" class="mw-redirect" title="Sturm, Ruger">Sturm, Ruger</a> – from its founders, <a href="/wiki/Alexander_McCormick_Sturm" title="Alexander McCormick Sturm">Alexander McCormick Sturm</a> and <a href="/wiki/William_B._Ruger" title="William B. Ruger">William B. Ruger</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/STX_(sports_manufacturer)" title="STX (sports manufacturer)">STX</a> – pronounced as the word "sticks" because, when first founded, STX manufactured only <a href="/wiki/Lacrosse_stick" title="Lacrosse stick">lacrosse sticks</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Subaru" title="Subaru">Subaru</a> – from the Japanese name for the constellation known to Westerners as <a href="/wiki/Pleiades" title="Pleiades">Pleiades</a> or the Seven Sisters. Subaru's parent company, <a href="/wiki/Fuji_Heavy_Industries" class="mw-redirect" title="Fuji Heavy Industries">Fuji Heavy Industries</a>, was formed from a merger of six companies, and the constellation is featured on the company's logo.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sumazi" title="Sumazi">Sumazi</a> – social data intelligence company named after its Bangladeshi-American founder <a href="/wiki/Sumaya_Kazi" title="Sumaya Kazi"><b>Sum</b>aya K<b>azi</b></a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sun_Microsystems" title="Sun Microsystems">Sun Microsystems</a> – its founders designed their first <a href="/wiki/Workstation" title="Workstation">workstation</a> in their dorm at <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford University</a>, and chose the name <i>Stanford University Network</i> for their product, hoping to sell it to the college. They did not. The company was taken over by <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Corporation" title="Oracle Corporation">Oracle Corporation</a> in 2010.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/SUSE" title="SUSE">SuSE</a> – from <b>S</b>oftware <b>u</b>nd <b>S</b>ystem-<b>E</b>ntwicklung (software and system development). The company was bought by Novell for its Linux distribution.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Suzuki" title="Suzuki">Suzuki</a> – automotive giant named after its founder, Michio Suzuki. The company started as Suzuki Loom Works in Japan in 1909, and entered the motorcycle market in the early 1950s. It changed its name to Suzuki Motor Co., Ltd in 1954.</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="T">T</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_company_name_etymologies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: T">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Taco_Bell" title="Taco Bell">Taco Bell</a> – named after founder Glen Bell</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Techniques_d%27Avant_Garde" title="Techniques d'Avant Garde">TAG Group (Holdings) S.A.</a> – Luxembourg-based holding company named from <b>T</b>echniques d'<b>A</b>vant <b>G</b>arde</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/TAG_Heuer" title="TAG Heuer">TAG Heuer</a> – watch-maker named after Edouard Heuer, who founded Uhrenmanufaktur Heuer AG in Switzerland in 1860<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> It was taken over by <a href="/wiki/Techniques_d%27Avant_Garde" title="Techniques d'Avant Garde">TAG Group (Holdings) S.A.</a> in 1985 and branded TAG Heuer in 1999. It is now owned by the <a href="/wiki/LVMH" title="LVMH">LVMH</a> (Louis Vuitton Moët Hennessy) conglomerate.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Talgo" title="Talgo">Talgo</a> – from "<b>T</b>ren <b>A</b>rticulado <b>L</b>igero <b>G</b>oicoechea-<b>O</b>riol" (Spanish for "Goicoechea-Oriol Light Articulated Train"), Goicoechea and Oriol being the founders of the company.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tallink" title="Tallink">Tallink</a> - from the Estonian capital <a href="/wiki/Tallinn" title="Tallinn"><b>Tallin</b>n</a> and the word "<b>link</b>" as the company links Tallinn with other cities by the sea.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tama_Drums" title="Tama Drums">Tama Drums</a> – Tama was the name of the owner's wife, and means "jewel" in Japanese.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/TAM_Airlines" class="mw-redirect" title="TAM Airlines">TAM Airlines</a> – named from <b>T</b>ransportes <b>A</b>éreos <b>M</b>arília (Marilia's Air Transport). Marília is a city in São Paulo state, Brazil</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/TAP_Portugal" class="mw-redirect" title="TAP Portugal">TAP Portugal</a> – from "<b>T</b>ransportes <b>A</b>éreos <b>P</b>ortugueses" (Portuguese Air Transport).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Targray" title="Targray">Targray</a> – a portmanteau of founder <b>T</b>homas <b>A</b>ndrew <b>R</b>ichardson's initials and his mother's maiden name. (Gray)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Taser_International" class="mw-redirect" title="Taser International">Taser International</a> – named after a fictional weapon, <b>T</b>homas <b>A</b>. <b>S</b>wift's <b>E</b>lectric <b>R</b>ifle, after the novel <i><a href="/wiki/Tom_Swift_and_His_Electric_Rifle" title="Tom Swift and His Electric Rifle">Tom Swift and His Electric Rifle</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Victor_Appleton" title="Victor Appleton">Victor Appleton</a>. The company was incorporated in Arizona in 1993 by brothers Rick and Tom Smith as Air Taser, Inc.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Taxan" title="Taxan">Taxan</a> – made-up name chosen partly because Takusan is a Japanese word for <i>many</i> or <i>much</i> and was considered propitious, but mainly because the head of the company, in the U.S. at the time, Tak Shimizu was known by everyone as <b>Tak-san</b>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/TCBY" title="TCBY">TCBY</a> – originally, the company's name was "This Can't Be Yogurt", but a lawsuit from a competitor named "I Can't Believe It's Yogurt!" forced TCBY to create a new backronym for its initials: "The Country's Best Yogurt".</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/TCL_Corporation" title="TCL Corporation">TCL</a> – from <b>T</b>oday <b>C</b>hina <b>L</b>ion. Derived from literal translation of "今日中国雄狮" from Chinese to English.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/TDK_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="TDK Corporation">TDK Corporation</a> – from <b>T</b>okyo <b>D</b>enki <b>K</b>agaku (Tokyo Electronics and Chemicals)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Textron" title="Textron">Textron</a> – this U.S. defense conglomerate was founded as the Special Yarns Corporation in 1923 and later traded as Atlantic Rayon Corporation, when its main business was parachutes. After World War II, it moved into lingerie and other consumer goods, and needed a new name. The company history says: "Atlantic Rayon's advertising agency suggested Señorita Creations, but it was rejected in favor of Textron. The 'Tex' was derived from <b>tex</b>tiles and the 'tron' came from synthetics such as Lus<b>tron</b>."<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> Textron bought <a href="/wiki/Bell_Aerospace" class="mw-redirect" title="Bell Aerospace">Bell Aerospace</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Cessna_Aircraft_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Cessna Aircraft Company">Cessna Aircraft Company</a>, among many others.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Electric_Power_Company" title="Tokyo Electric Power Company">TEPCO</a> – <b>T</b>okyo <b>E</b>lectric <b>P</b>ower <b>Co</b>mpany</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tesco" title="Tesco">Tesco</a> – founder Jack <b>Co</b>hen, who sold groceries in the markets of the <a href="/wiki/London_East_End" class="mw-redirect" title="London East End">London East End</a> from 1919, acquired a large shipment of tea from <b>T. E. S</b>tockwell. He made new labels by using the first three letters of the supplier's name and the first two letters of his surname.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tesla,_Inc." title="Tesla, Inc.">Tesla</a> – Named after Serbian <a href="/wiki/Electrical_engineer" class="mw-redirect" title="Electrical engineer">electrical engineer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Physicist" title="Physicist">physicist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nikola_Tesla" title="Nikola Tesla">Nikola Tesla</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Tesla_background_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tesla_background-120">[120]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> The Tesla Roadster uses an <a href="/wiki/AC_motor" title="AC motor">AC motor</a> descended directly from Nikola Tesla's original 1882 design.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Naot" title="Naot">Teva Naot</a> – outdoors shoe company is named after the modern Hebrew word for 'nature' (pronounced "tehvah")</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Texaco" title="Texaco">Texaco</a> – from The <b>Texa</b>s <b>Co</b>mpany U.S.A.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/THX" title="THX">THX</a> – from <a href="/wiki/Tomlinson_Holman" title="Tomlinson Holman">Tomlinson Holman</a> Crossover, the name of the technology's inventor and the audio technology of a "crossover" amplifier. It may be a <a href="/wiki/Backronym" title="Backronym">backronym</a>, as the technology was created by <a href="/wiki/George_Lucas" title="George Lucas">George Lucas</a>'s then-company, <a href="/wiki/Lucasfilm" title="Lucasfilm">Lucasfilm</a>, and he directed <i><a href="/wiki/THX_1138" title="THX 1138">THX 1138</a></i>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Turkish_Airlines" title="Turkish Airlines">THY</a> – Turkish Airlines. THY is the abbreviation of <i><b>T</b>ürk <b>H</b>ava <b>Y</b>olları</i>, which means Turkish Air Ways in Turkish.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/TIBCO_Software" title="TIBCO Software">TIBCO Software</a> – <b>T</b>he <b>I</b>nformation <b>B</b>us <b>Co</b>mpany. The company was founded by Vivek Ranadive as Teknekron Software Systems in 1985.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tim_Hortons" title="Tim Hortons">Tim Hortons</a> – Canadian fast food doughnut, sandwich and coffee shop named after founder and hockey player <b><a href="/wiki/Tim_Horton" title="Tim Horton">Tim Horton</a></b>. In Canada Tim Hortons is nicknamed "Tim's" and "Timmy's"; in America, the chain is nicknamed "Timmy Ho's". The name was changed from Tim Horton's, dropping the apostrophe, to preclude legal action in Quebec where businesses are obliged to use French language names.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/TNT_N.V." title="TNT N.V.">TNT N.V.</a> and <a href="/wiki/TNT_Express" title="TNT Express">TNT Express</a> – <b>T</b>homas <b>N</b>ationwide <b>T</b>ransport, an Australian company which was acquired by the Dutch postal company in 1996. The postal company renamed itself TNT N.V. in 2005. In 2011, TNT N.V. demerged; the express delivery company took the name TNT Express while the postal company renamed itself <a href="/wiki/PostNL" title="PostNL">PostNL</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Toshiba" title="Toshiba">Toshiba</a> – named from the merger of consumer goods company <b>To</b>kyo Denki (Tokyo Electric Co) and electrical firm <b>Shiba</b>ura Seisaku-sho (Shibaura Engineering Works).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Toyota" title="Toyota">Toyota</a> – from the name of the founder, Sakichi Toyoda. Initially called Toyeda, it was changed after a contest for a better-sounding name. The new name was written in <a href="/wiki/Katakana" title="Katakana">katakana</a> with eight strokes, a number that is considered lucky in Japan.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Trader_Joe%27s" title="Trader Joe's">Trader Joe's</a> – named after the grocery store's founder, <a href="/wiki/Joe_Coulombe" title="Joe Coulombe">Joe Coulombe</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tronc" class="mw-redirect" title="Tronc">Tronc</a> – In 2016, US-based media corporation Tribune Publishing changed its name to Tronc – short for <b>Tr</b>ibune <b>on</b>line <b>c</b>ontent<sup id="cite_ref-auto_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-126">[126]</a></sup>. In 2018, the company changed it back.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lines_Bros" title="Lines Bros">Triang</a> – operating name for Lines Bros Ltd, which was founded by William, Walter and Arthur Edwin Lines. Three Lines make a <b>triang</b>le</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/TSMC" title="TSMC">TSMC</a> – <b>T</b>aiwan <b>S</b>emiconductor <b>M</b>anufacturing <b>C</b>ompany, an independent chip foundry founded in Taiwan in 1987.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tucows" title="Tucows">Tucows</a> – acronym for <b>T</b>he <b>U</b>ltimate <b>C</b>ollection <b>O</b>f <b>W</b>insock <b>S</b>oftware.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tungsram" title="Tungsram">Tungsram</a> – derived from <b>Tungs</b>ten + Wolf<b>ram</b>, two variations of the name of the main raw material of the lamp production.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/TVR" title="TVR">TVR</a> – derived from the first name of the company founder <b>T</b>re<b>V</b>o<b>R</b> Wilkinson</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/TWA" class="mw-redirect" title="TWA">TWA</a> – derived from <b>T</b>rans <b>W</b>orld <b>A</b>irlines.  Before the airline opened up its first international route from New York to Paris in the 1950s, it was a domestic operation that focused on serving Los Angeles and San Francisco from New York, operating under the name <b>T</b>ranscontinental and <b>W</b>estern <b>A</b>ir.  Keeping the initials and rebranding as a global airline was a stroke of marketing continuity genius.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Twinings" title="Twinings">Twinings</a> – named after founder Thomas Twining, who set up a tea-shop on the Strand in London in 1706.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> – having rejected the name Twitch for their <a href="/wiki/Social_networking" class="mw-redirect" title="Social networking">social networking</a> service, co-founder <a href="/wiki/Jack_Dorsey" title="Jack Dorsey">Jack Dorsey</a> says: "we looked in the dictionary for words around it and we came across the word 'twitter' and it was just perfect. The definition was 'a short burst of inconsequential information', and 'chirps from birds'. And that's exactly what the product was."<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="U">U</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_company_name_etymologies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: U">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/UBS" title="UBS">UBS</a> – named from the initials of the <b>U</b>nion <b>B</b>ank of <b>S</b>witzerland, which merged with the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Bank_Corporation" title="Swiss Bank Corporation">Swiss Bank Corporation</a> (SBC) in 1998. The initials no longer stand for anything, says the company,<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> possibly because "United Bank of Switzerland" might be confused with the United Bank's subsidiary, United Bank Switzerland.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Umbro" title="Umbro">Umbro</a> – Umbro was founded in 1924 by the Humphrey (<b>Um</b>phrey) <b>Bro</b>thers, Harold C. and Wallace.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Unilever" title="Unilever">Unilever</a> – name created to reflect the merger of Margarine <b>Uni</b>e and <b>Lever</b> Brothers, agreed in 1929. <a href="/wiki/Lever_Brothers" title="Lever Brothers">Lever Brothers</a> was named after its founders, <a href="/wiki/William_Hesketh_Lever" class="mw-redirect" title="William Hesketh Lever">William Hesketh Lever</a> and his brother, James.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Unimed_(organization)" title="Unimed (organization)">UNIMED</a> – Brazilian <a href="/wiki/Cooperative" title="Cooperative">cooperative</a> of physicians, meaning <b>Uni</b>ão de <b>Med</b>icos (Physicians' Union)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Unisys" title="Unisys">Unisys</a> – from <b>Un</b>ited <b>I</b>nformation <b>Sys</b>tems, the new name for the company that resulted from the merging of two old mainframe computer companies, Burroughs and Sperry [Sperry Univac/Sperry Rand]. It <i>united</i> two incompatible ranges. The newborn Unisys was briefly the world's second-largest computer company, after IBM.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Unocal_Corporation" title="Unocal Corporation">Unocal Corporation</a> – the <b>Un</b>ion <b>O</b>il Company of <b>Cal</b>ifornia, founded in 1890</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/United_Parcel_Service" title="United Parcel Service">UPS</a> – <b>U</b>nited <b>P</b>arcel <b>S</b>ervice of America, Inc.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/UUNET" title="UUNET">UUNET</a> – one of the industry's oldest and largest Internet Service Providers, named from <b>U</b>NIX-to-<b>U</b>NIX <b>Net</b>work</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="V">V</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_company_name_etymologies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: V">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Vaisala" title="Vaisala">Vaisala</a> – Finnish company named after its founder, Professor <a href="/wiki/Vilho_V%C3%A4is%C3%A4l%C3%A4" title="Vilho Väisälä">Vilho Väisälä</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Valero_Energy_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Valero Energy Corporation">Valero Energy Corporation</a> – from <i>Misión San Antonio de Valero</i>, the Spanish-language name of the mission in the company's home city better known as <a href="/wiki/Alamo_Mission_in_San_Antonio" title="Alamo Mission in San Antonio">The Alamo</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Valtra" title="Valtra">Valtra</a> – from <b>Val</b>met <b>Tra</b>ctors, where <a href="/wiki/Valmet" title="Valmet">Valmet</a> is the name of a Finnish state-owned company (originally "Valtion Metallitehtaat" – English: "State Metalworks")</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Valve_Corporation" title="Valve Corporation">Valve Corporation</a> – game development company who uses a valve as symbolism, as in a lever which makes the flow of ideas readily accessible</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Varig" title="Varig">Varig</a> – <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazilian</a> airline, its name is an abbreviation of <i><b>V</b>iação <b>A</b>érea <b>R</b>io-<b>G</b>randense</i>, because it was founded in the state of <a href="/wiki/Rio_Grande_do_Sul" title="Rio Grande do Sul">Rio Grande do Sul</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Verizon_Communications" title="Verizon Communications">Verizon</a> – portmanteau of <b>ver</b>itas (Latin for <i>truth</i>) and hor<b>izon</b>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Verkkokauppa.com" title="Verkkokauppa.com">Verkkokauppa.com</a> – directly from the company's official URL. "Verkkokauppa" translates to "Internet store" in <a href="/wiki/Finnish_language" title="Finnish language">Finnish</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Victorinox" title="Victorinox">Victorinox</a> – derived from the name of the founder's mother, Victoria, and a <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> abbreviation for <a href="/wiki/Stainless_steel" title="Stainless steel">stainless steel</a>, inox. Known for their <a href="/wiki/Swiss_army_knife" class="mw-redirect" title="Swiss army knife">Swiss army knife</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Viking_Line" title="Viking Line">Viking Line</a> – from the prefix "Viking" appearing in the names of all the ships of <a href="/wiki/Rederi_Ab_Sally" title="Rederi Ab Sally">Rederi Ab Sally</a>, Viking Line's predecessor company.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Virb" title="Virb">Virb</a> – play on "verb", representing an action word in order to describe the product's users as "people who create"<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Virgin_Group" title="Virgin Group">Virgin</a> – founder <a href="/wiki/Richard_Branson" title="Richard Branson">Richard Branson</a> started a magazine called <i>Student</i> while still at school. In his autobiography, Losing My Virginity, Branson says that when they were starting a business to sell records by mail order, "one of the girls suggested: 'What about Virgin? We're complete virgins at business.'"</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/VMware_Inc." class="mw-redirect" title="VMware Inc.">VMware</a> – <b>V</b>irtual <b>M</b>achine [soft]ware</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Vodafone" title="Vodafone">Vodafone</a> – from <b>Vo</b>ice, <b>Da</b>ta, Tele<b>fone</b>. Vodafone made the UK's first mobile call at a few minutes past midnight on 1 January 1985.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Volkswagen" title="Volkswagen">Volkswagen</a> – from the German for "people's car". <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Porsche" title="Ferdinand Porsche">Ferdinand Porsche</a> wanted to produce a car that was affordable for the masses – the <i>Kraft-durch-Freude-Wagen</i> (or "Strength-Through-Joy car", from a Nazi social organization) later became known, in English, as the <i>Beetle</i>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Volvo" title="Volvo">Volvo</a> – from the Latin word "volvo", which means "I roll". It was originally a name for a ball bearing being developed by <a href="/wiki/SKF" title="SKF">SKF</a> (<i>Svenska Kullagerfabriken AB</i> or, in English, Swedish ball bearing factory).</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="W">W</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_company_name_etymologies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: W">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Wachovia" title="Wachovia">Wachovia</a> – from the Latin version of the German <b>wachau</b>, the name given to a region in North Carolina by Moravian settlers because it reminded them of the Austrian valley of Wachau, through which the Danube River flows. Wachovia Bank was founded in Winston-Salem, North Carolina, which is located in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Waitrose" class="mw-redirect" title="Waitrose">Waitrose</a> – upmarket UK supermarket chain originally named after the founders, Wallace <b>Wait</b>e, Arthur <b>Rose</b> and David Taylor. The "Taylor" was later dropped.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Walgreens" title="Walgreens">Walgreens</a> – named after founder Charles R. Walgreen, Sr.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Walmart" title="Walmart">Wal-Mart</a> – named after founder Sam <b>Wal</b>ton</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/The_Walt_Disney_Company" title="The Walt Disney Company">The Walt Disney Company</a> – named for its co-founder <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney" title="Walt Disney">Walt Disney</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wang_Laboratories" title="Wang Laboratories">Wang Laboratories</a> – from the name of the founder, <a href="/wiki/An_Wang" title="An Wang">An Wang</a>, the inventor of core memory.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wells_Fargo" title="Wells Fargo">Wells Fargo</a> – from the founders of the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Wells_Fargo" title="History of Wells Fargo">original Wells Fargo company</a>, <a href="/wiki/Henry_Wells" title="Henry Wells">Henry Wells</a> and <a href="/wiki/William_G._Fargo" class="mw-redirect" title="William G. Fargo">William G. Fargo</a>.(When <a href="/wiki/Norwest_Corporation" title="Norwest Corporation">Norwest Corporation</a> purchased Wells Fargo in 1998, it chose to retain the Wells Fargo name.)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wendy%27s" title="Wendy's">Wendy's</a> – Wendy was the nickname of founder <a href="/wiki/Dave_Thomas_(businessman)" title="Dave Thomas (businessman)">Dave Thomas</a>' daughter Melinda.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Weta_Digital" title="Weta Digital">Weta Digital</a> – special effects company co-founded by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)" title="The Lord of the Rings (film series)">The Lord of the Rings</a></i> director Peter Jackson. <a href="/wiki/Weta" title="Weta">Weta</a> are a group of about 70 species of insect found in New Zealand, where Weta Digital is based.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/W_H_Smith" class="mw-redirect" title="W H Smith">W H Smith</a> – founded by Henry Walton Smith and his wife Anna in London, England, in 1792. They named their small <a href="/wiki/Newsagent%27s_shop" title="Newsagent's shop">newsagent's shop</a> after their son <b>W</b>illiam <b>H</b>enry <b>Smith</b>, who was born the same year.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Williams-Sonoma" title="Williams-Sonoma">Williams-Sonoma</a> – founded by <a href="/wiki/Chuck_Williams_(author)" title="Chuck Williams (author)">Chuck Williams</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sonoma,_California" title="Sonoma, California">Sonoma</a>, California.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wolfram_Research" title="Wolfram Research">Wolfram Research</a> – named after computer scientist <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Wolfram" title="Stephen Wolfram">Stephen Wolfram</a>, who founded the company in 1987 before launching <a href="/wiki/Mathematica" class="mw-redirect" title="Mathematica">Mathematica</a> software in 1988<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wonderware" title="Wonderware">Wonderware</a> – from <b>Wonder</b>ful Soft<b>ware</b> - Wonderware was the project code name for the company prior to its launch. Upon making the company a legal entity, the code name was retained as the company name.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Worlds_of_Wonder_(toy_company)" title="Worlds of Wonder (toy company)">Worlds of Wonder</a> – founder Don Kingsborough wanted an eyecatching stock symbol, and Worlds of Wonder provided WOW. The company went bankrupt in 1988.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/WPP_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="WPP Group">WPP</a> – global advertising and marketing company founded by <a href="/wiki/Martin_Sorrell" title="Martin Sorrell">Martin Sorrell</a> in 1985. He bought an existing listed company, <b>W</b>ire &amp; <b>P</b>lastic <b>P</b>roducts PLC, to use as a shell.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/WWE" title="WWE">WWE</a> – from the company's legal name of World Wrestling Entertainment, adopted in 2002; it began using the initialism as its trading name in 2011. The previous name of World Wrestling Federation (WWF), used since 1979, was changed after a court case brought by the World Wildlife Fund (WWF), which is now called the <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Fund_for_Nature" title="World Wide Fund for Nature">World Wide Fund for Nature</a>.</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="X">X</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_company_name_etymologies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: X">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Xerox" title="Xerox">Xerox</a> – named from xerography, a word derived from the Greek <i>xeros</i> (dry) and <i>graphos</i> (writing). The company was founded as The Haloid Company in 1906, launched its first XeroX copier in 1949, and changed its name to Haloid Xerox in 1958.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Xiaomi" title="Xiaomi">Xiaomi</a> – <i>Xiaomi</i> is the Chinese word for "<a href="/wiki/History_of_Xiaomi#Etymology" title="History of Xiaomi">millet</a>".</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/XIX_Entertainment" title="XIX Entertainment">XIX Entertainment</a> – XIX is 19 in Roman numerals, so the company is named indirectly after Paul Hardcastle's single 19, and directly derived from <a href="/wiki/19_Entertainment" title="19 Entertainment">19 Entertainment</a> – see above.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Xobni" title="Xobni">Xobni</a> – "inbox", spelled backwards</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Xstrata" title="Xstrata">Xstrata</a> – name for a Swiss global mining and extraction company, formerly known as Sudelektra. The name is derived from the terms "extraction" and "strata" (sedimentary levels). The name was created in 1999 by <a href="/wiki/John_Lloyd_(graphic_designer)" title="John Lloyd (graphic designer)">John Lloyd</a> of the design consultancy, Lloyd Northover.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/XTO_Energy" title="XTO Energy">XTO Energy</a> – founded in 1986 as Cross Timbers Oil Company, it went public under the stock ticker XTO, and changed its name to XTO Energy Inc in 2001. It is now owned by <a href="/wiki/ExxonMobil" title="ExxonMobil">ExxonMobil</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Y">Y</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_company_name_etymologies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Y">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Yahoo!" title="Yahoo!">Yahoo!</a> – word <i>Yahoo</i> was invented by <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Swift" title="Jonathan Swift">Jonathan Swift</a> and used in his book <i><a href="/wiki/Gulliver%27s_Travels" title="Gulliver's Travels">Gulliver's Travels</a></i>. It represents a person who is repulsive in appearance and barely human. Yahoo! founders <a href="/wiki/David_Filo" title="David Filo">David Filo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Yang_(entrepreneur)" class="mw-redirect" title="Jerry Yang (entrepreneur)">Jerry Yang</a> jokingly considered themselves yahoos. It's also an interjection sometimes associated with United States Southerners' and Westerners' expression of joy, as alluded to in Yahoo.com commercials that end with someone singing the word "yahoo". It is also sometime jokingly referred to by its <a href="/wiki/Backronym" title="Backronym">backronym</a>, <b>Y</b>et <b>A</b>nother <b>H</b>ierarchical <b>O</b>fficious <b>O</b>racle.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/YKK" title="YKK">YKK</a> – zipper manufacturer named from <b>Y</b>oshida <b>K</b>ogyo <b>K</b>abushikikaisha (<i>Yoshida Company Limited</i>) after the founder, Tadao Yoshida. The letters YKK were stamped onto the zippers' pull tabs.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Yakult" title="Yakult">Yakult</a> – official claims state that the name is derived from jahurto, an older form of jogurto, the <a href="/wiki/Esperanto" title="Esperanto">Esperanto</a> word for "yogurt". However, it has also been claimed that the name is derived from the fact that the product was developed from ancient Mongolian practices of culturing yak's milk in a sack made from a yak's stomach – the combination of Yak and Culture in English giving the product name as "Yakult".</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Yamaha" class="mw-redirect" title="Yamaha">Yamaha</a> – after Torakusu Yamaha, who founded the company as <i>Nippon Gakki Seizō Kabushiki Gaisha</i> (Japan Musical Instrument Manufacturing Corporation) in 1897 after repairing a reed organ. The name was changed to Yamaha Corporation on 1 October 1987.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Yoplait" title="Yoplait">Yoplait</a> – from the merger of <b>Yo</b>la and Co<b>plait</b> in 1965<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Z">Z</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_company_name_etymologies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Z">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Zamzar" title="Zamzar">Zamzar</a> – based on the main character <a href="/wiki/Gregor_Samsa" class="mw-redirect" title="Gregor Samsa">Gregor Samsa</a> (Gregor S<b>am</b>s<b>a</b>) from <a href="/wiki/Franz_Kafka" title="Franz Kafka">Franz Kafka</a>'s story <i><a href="/wiki/The_Metamorphosis" title="The Metamorphosis">The Metamorphosis</a></i>. Kafka describes a young man who is transformed whilst sleeping into a monstrous verminous bug. A version of the man's name was used as the basis for the company name because of its powerful association with change and transformation.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Zend_Technologies" title="Zend Technologies">Zend Technologies</a> – contraction derived from the names of <b>Ze</b>ev Suraski and A<b>nd</b>i Gutmans, the two founders</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Zero_Halliburton" title="Zero Halliburton">Zero Corporation</a> – Founded by Herman Zierold as Zierold Metal Corporation, it is the parent company of <a href="/wiki/Zero_Halliburton" title="Zero Halliburton">Zero Halliburton</a>. In 1952, when then owner Jack Gilbert noticed that many of the company's customers mispronounced and misspelled "Zierold" as "Zero," he changed the name of the company to Zero Manufacturing.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/ZF_Friedrichshafen" title="ZF Friedrichshafen">ZF Group</a> – car parts manufacturer named from <b>Z</b>ahnrad<b>f</b>abrik, the German for Gear Factory.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Zimmer,_Inc." class="mw-redirect" title="Zimmer, Inc.">Zimmer</a> – named after Justin O. Zimmer, who co-founded the medical equipment company in Warsaw, Indiana, in 1927.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Zuse" class="mw-redirect" title="Zuse">Zuse</a> – pioneering German computer company named after its founder, Konrad <b>Zuse</b> (1910–1995). He built his first computer in his parents' living room at the end of the 1930s. Zuse was taken over by <a href="/wiki/Siemens_AG" class="mw-redirect" title="Siemens AG">Siemens AG</a>. The name is now supposedly echoed by <a href="/wiki/SuSE" class="mw-redirect" title="SuSE">SuSE</a> (<b>S</b>oftware <b>u</b>nd <b>S</b>ystem-<b>E</b>ntwicklung: "Software and system development").</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Zynga" title="Zynga">Zynga</a> – named after founder <a href="/wiki/Mark_Pincus" title="Mark Pincus">Mark Pincus</a>'s <a href="/wiki/American_bulldog" class="mw-redirect" title="American bulldog">American bulldog</a>, Zinga<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_company_name_etymologies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
